After the Opening of Sino-Japanese Air Routes in North China, It Is No Different from Exclusive Military Flights for the Japanese. The Kwantung Army Plans to Expand Air Routes Again. Traitor Yin Again Occupies Xinhe Salt Flats 89

Tianjin Correspondence: It has been half a month since the opening of Sino-Japanese air routes in North China on November 18. In these forty-five days, the aviation business operated under the name of the Huitong Company has shown no improvement. The four routes originally planned with Tianjin as the central hub - Tianjin-Dalian, Tianjin-Jinzhou, Tianjin-Chengde, and Tianjin-Zhangjiakou - have seen very few passengers on the latter three routes, despite the specified routes. Recently, they have become irregular routes. Even on the Tianjin-Dalian route, most of the passengers are Japanese, mostly army and navy personnel, with very few Chinese. Because the pseudo-Manchukuo does not allow Chinese to enter and exit freely, those with business in that area are unwilling to risk going by air and are often restricted. The irregular flights on the Tianjin-Chengde, Tianjin-Jinzhou, and Tianjin-Zhangjiakou routes are mostly due to the lack of ordinary passengers. Therefore, Huitong is nominally a privately-run airline, but in reality, it is still an air squadron under the command of Lieutenant Colonel Higuchi of the Japanese military department. Zhang Yunrong, the chairman of the company, has been claiming illness and has returned to Peiping since the opening of the routes. He has not returned to Tianjin even after nearly fifty days. The reason for this is nothing more than the difficulty of handling affairs, and the measures taken by the counterpart are not fully compliant with the various regulations concluded in the agreement. A few days ago, the commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army, O, announced that between February and March of next year, the Manchuria Aviation Company and the Huitong Company will jointly connect the Tianjin-Changchun and Tianjin-Harbin air routes, with Jinzhou, Dalian, and Chengde as exchange stations. There will be three round trips per week. These two routes will then form an air route network between North China and Manchuria. If realized, transportation will become more convenient. The air route connecting Dalian with Japan will also be held between April and May, with Fukuoka as the central exchange station. Departing in the morning and arriving in the evening, it will take only ten hours to travel from Tokyo to Tianjin, or from Tianjin to Tokyo. The aircraft currently operating between Tianjin and Dalian is only one Ford-style eight-seat three-engine aircraft. Huitong Company has ordered one A.T. type eight-seat super-speed all-metal aircraft from the Nakajima Aircraft Manufacturing Plant in Osaka, which will be completed in February of next year. It will be used to operate the Tianjin-Dalian section and for connecting flights to Fukuoka. The aircraft will be able to fly from Tianjin to Dalian in one hour, shortening the time by about one hour compared to the current aircraft. The aircraft will have smoking and washing facilities, making it more modern than the current types of aircraft. The company's capital was originally set at 5.4 million yuan. In addition to the 2.7 million yuan that has already been raised, the remaining amount is being raised to expand operations and purchase aircraft. The Hebei-Chahar Political Council should be responsible for 1.35 million yuan, which will be raised by the Hebei Provincial Bank. There has been no contact with our postal authorities regarding the attachment of mail, but in fact, the company has been collecting and sending it on its own, and parcels are also transported at will. The only difference is that it has not publicly announced the collection and sending of mail. It is said that when the various joint air routes are completed in April of next year, the company will officially operate its own postal air service. The Tanggu salt flats under the jurisdiction of the Changlu Salt Transport Administration were occupied by the Japanese military headquarters in October of this year and designated as military land. After many negotiations, the stakes and nets have not been removed. There are various rumors about what the land will be used for. This matter has not been resolved. Yesterday, we received a report from the salt flat residents of Xinhe, stating that the pseudo-government of eastern Hebei has notified the salt flats that it intends to occupy the flats on New Year's Day, and will sell the salt produced there itself. In addition to reporting to the Ministry of Finance as quickly as possible to find a way to negotiate and stop it, the Changlu Salt Transport Administration has also cancelled the 100,000 yuan of subsidies per month, which had been privately agreed with the pseudo-regime since this spring, with the condition that the salt flats would not be disturbed, to show its resistance. Based on all of this, it is predictable that this matter will not be easily resolved. As for the pseudo-government's takeover of the salt flats, it is rumored to be at the instigation of a certain party, because that party urgently needs Changlu salt to produce chemical salt. This year, 70,000 tons were transported there. Next year, it is planned to purchase 250,000 tons. Fearing that it would affect the people's food supply, we did not agree. The party then instigated the pseudo-government to forcibly take over, in order to facilitate the purchase of goods. (30th)

Linhe Correspondence: Linhe is located on the western border of Sui Province, at the junction of Sui, Ningxia, and western Mongolia. Beijing Seriously Cleans Up Opium and Drugs: New Regulations for Drug Prohibition and Punishment Determined to Be Implemented on New Year's Day; Mayor Ma Reports on Beijing's Drug Prohibition Progress 91

Nanjing dispatch: The municipal government held a memorial service for the Premier at 8 a.m. on the 28th. All staff members attended. After Mayor Ma, as chairman, led the ceremony, he delivered a report on the spot. He began by saying, "In the past two weeks, people across the country and in various countries around the world have expressed their grief and concern over the ordeal of Chairman Chiang. Fortunately, Chairman Chiang's great personality inspired Zhang, Yang and others to thoroughly repent. This unprecedented incident was eliminated invisibly. Now the leader has safely returned to Nanjing the day before yesterday. The whole country is celebrating, a grand occasion unprecedented since the founding of the Republic. Although our losses in this incident are not small, the gains are also extremely great. This incident proves that the entire country, regardless of whether they were usually dissatisfied with the leader, the Party, or the government, could unanimously work hard to rescue the leader from danger, support the government, and support the Party. This is sufficient proof that the country has a very solid foundation, and the nation has an extremely cohesive unity. In the future, anyone who wants to harm the Party, the country, or the leader will undoubtedly fail. However, while we are celebrating the leader's escape from danger, we should not forget the seriousness of the national crisis. We should work together to 'strive forward to break through the national crisis and revive the nation.'" Mayor Ma continued, "The year 25 is coming to an end, and the year 26 is about to begin. The government's newly formulated regulations for drug prohibition, opium prohibition, and punishment will be strictly enforced in a few days. Therefore, I specially report this, hoping that all citizens will pay special attention. The government has spared no effort in publicizing and promoting drug and opium prohibition for the past three to four years. Our city first established a drug rehabilitation hospital in the 23rd year. The number of beds gradually increased from 150 to 2,270. By the end of January of the 24th year, as the number of opium addicts gradually decreased, the drug rehabilitation hospital was merged into one location at Chaotian Palace. After June of this year, due to special circumstances, the drug rehabilitation hospital was moved to Chaoku Street and Chuanban Lane successively, with a total of 750 beds. As for the expenditures, from the establishment on February 9th of the 23rd year to October of this year, a total of more than 178,600 yuan was spent. A total of 22,728 opium addicts have been discharged after successful rehabilitation. There are still more than 700 opium addicts currently undergoing rehabilitation. However, there are still many citizens in the city who smoke opium and have not undergone rehabilitation. Nanjing is an absolutely opium-free area, and it is still like this. The situation in other places can be imagined. The reason for this is that the general public regards government policies as mere formalities. At the same time, they are afraid of difficulties and procrastinate, leading to this situation. The harm of opium and drugs is known to everyone and does not need to be repeated. Now, in addition to using military force and economic aggression, the enemy is using the most vicious and cruel poisoning policy, smuggling large quantities of heroin, morphine, and other drugs to lure our people into addiction in order to realize their ambition to destroy our country and exterminate our race. This kind of poisoning policy is more harmful than any other aggressive policy. Once the people are poisoned, their bodies and minds will undergo various changes. Neurologically, there are symptoms such as selfishness, forgetfulness, dishonesty, lying, and deception. Physically, there are symptoms such as constipation, heart weakness, and slow breathing. Its toxicity can also be passed on to future generations, causing endless harm. Now, countries around the world are striving for eugenics. How can we not thoroughly eliminate this kind of opium and drugs that weaken the country and the race in order to eliminate the obstacles to strong countries and strong races? As the saying goes, there is no greater sorrow than the death of the heart. The enemy's poisoning policy is precisely intended to kill our hearts. Therefore, in order to save the country and revive the nation, the government has decided to strictly enforce drug and opium prohibition. From New Year's Day of the 26th year, new regulations for drug prohibition, opium prohibition, and punishment will be implemented. Here are the most important articles for reporting: (1) Article 8 of the Drug Prohibition and Punishment Regulations: From the 26th year of the Republic of China, those who commit the crimes in Articles 3 to 7 of these regulations (i.e., manufacturing, transporting, selling, or using drugs, or administering morphine injections to others) shall be sentenced to death. (2) Article 5 of the Opium Prohibition and Punishment Regulations: Those who transport, sell, or possess opium with the intention of selling it shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for not less than five years, and may also be fined not more than 3,000 yuan. If the quantity is more than 500 taels, the sentence shall be death. Those who transport, sell, or possess poppy seeds with the intention of selling them shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than ten years, and may also be fined not more than 1,000 yuan. Those who import opium or poppy seeds from foreign countries shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for not less than ten years, and may also be fined not more than 5,000 yuan. The same applies to those who export them to foreign countries. Article 6: Those who set up places with the intention of making profits, providing opium and smoking paraphernalia for people to smoke, shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for not less than five years, and may also be fined not more than 3,000 yuan. Article 8: Those who smoke opium shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than six months and not more than two years, and may also be fined not more than 300 yuan. Addicts shall also be required to go to the hospital for compulsory rehabilitation within a time limit. Those who voluntarily surrender for rehabilitation and commit the aforementioned crime again shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than one year and not more than three years, and may also be fined not more than 500 yuan. Addicts shall still be required to go to the hospital for compulsory rehabilitation within a time limit. Those who commit the first crime again after compulsory rehabilitation shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than ten years, and may also be fined not more than 1,000 yuan. Addicts shall still be required to go to the hospital for compulsory rehabilitation within a time limit. Those who commit the crime for the third time shall be sentenced to death. School teachers, staff, and students who commit any of the above three crimes shall be punished according to the highest penalty for each item. There are only a few days left before New Year's Day of the 26th year. The critical moment of life and death is imminent. I hope that all those who smoke opium will wake up as soon as possible and voluntarily go to the drug rehabilitation hospital to request rehabilitation. You should know that the government will keep its word. Do not test the law with your own bodies and regret it too late. Finally, I hope that if any of my colleagues in this government smoke opium, they should inspect each other and quit as soon as possible. They should take on the responsibility of leadership for the citizens and persuade them at any time and anywhere in order to save themselves and others. We cannot bear to punish without teaching. In these few days, we should mobilize the entire staff to publicize to the citizens as much as possible so that opium and drugs can be completely eliminated in the shortest possible time. From now on, if we turn back and rely on our own efforts for regeneration, it will not be difficult for the country and the nation to achieve the goal of prosperity and revival in three to five years," he said.

Xiamen Inn Association Asks for the Abolition of the Water Police Subsidy Fee, Originally a Temporary Exaction, but the Provincial Government Regards It as a Local Tax 92

Xiamen dispatch: The Second Detachment of the Fujian Water Police stationed in Xiamen, due to insufficient funds this summer, decided with the Chamber of Commerce, innkeepers, and shipping companies through the detachment leader Zhang Xijie that overseas Chinese going abroad would pay an additional 5 jiao (0.5 yuan) of national currency as a subsidy fee for the water police when purchasing tickets. The inns would collect the fee on behalf of the water police and hand it over to the shipping companies, who would then transfer it to the Second Detachment of the Water Police. This has been implemented since September of this year. Each month, 5,000 to 6,000 overseas Chinese leave Xiamen. Calculated at 5 jiao per person, the monthly income is approximately between 2,500 and 3,000 yuan. Recently, the provincial government issued an order that all donations be collected by the Xiamen Municipal Government Finance Bureau. The Finance Bureau ordered the shipping companies and inns to directly hand over the subsidy fee they collected to the Finance Bureau. However, the shipping companies and inns believe that the subsidy fee was originally of a temporary nature and should not be considered a regular tax, placing a long-term burden on overseas Chinese going abroad. Therefore, they refused to collect the fee on behalf of the Finance Bureau. The Finance Bureau then sent personnel accompanied by water and land police to intercept overseas Chinese boarding ships at the docks and coasts to collect the fee. Although the overseas Chinese all paid the fee, they had many complaints. On the 27th, the Inn Association submitted a petition to the Finance Bureau, requesting that it be forwarded to the provincial government to clearly abolish the subsidy fee. The main points of the petition are: "(1) When the Second Detachment of the Water Police launched the subsidy fee, it was originally for the purpose of building electric boats and consolidating coastal defense, and it was a temporary measure. (2) It was agreed to temporarily collect the fee for six months and then abolish it. (3) Since December 1st, the fee has been directly collected by your bureau, becoming a local tax. (4) Most overseas Chinese going abroad are laborers, and they have to borrow money in every possible way for travel expenses. They have no way to pay this subsidy fee and have no doubt about it. Because they thought it was temporary, they reluctantly obeyed the order. Now that it has become a local tax, it is inevitable that it will go against the intention of caring for overseas Chinese. Please forward the situation to the provincial government and approve the clear abolition of the subsidy fee in order to comply with the feelings of the overseas Chinese." It has been investigated that the subsidy fee is actually a kind of exorbitant tax. Most of the Chinese who go abroad are laborers who are unemployed in China. Their travel expenses are usually borrowed. The burdens of boat tickets, passports, vaccinations, etc. are already huge. Moreover, the establishment of the subsidy fee was only at the intention of the Second Detachment of the Water Police. The permission of the shipping companies and inns was only obtained through the water police team's announcement that if there were no objections from overseas Chinese and relevant agencies and organizations within two weeks, the shipping companies and inns would collect the fee from passengers going abroad. There is no legal or rational basis for this. Moreover, the so-called "no objection from overseas Chinese" means that those who are going abroad have not yet started their journey, so how can they be qualified to object? Therefore, it is actually an illegal exorbitant tax that adds a burden to overseas Chinese going abroad. (December 30th)

Wuxi 94

公用脚踏车免捐

Public Bicycles Exempt from Donation

本邑各机关团体公用脚踏车免费给照一案、前经财建两厅、令饬本县建设局、一律照章征收、以裕捐收、建设局奉令后、当以上项免费车辆、历办有年、率予更张、事实上颇多窒碍、经声叙缘由呈省、请予继续免费、旋奉财建两厅指令、准予免捐、惟应查明各该团体需要情形、限制辆数、其免捐牌照、如移挂于私有脚踏车行驶、一经查出、即予吊销、不再发给、并处以捐额十倍之罚金、此外邮局·电报局·等公会、自二十六年元旦起、一律纳捐领照、

The case of free licenses for public bicycles used by various agencies and organizations in this county was previously ordered by the Finance and Construction Departments to be collected by the County Construction Bureau in accordance with the regulations in order to increase donation revenue. After receiving the order, the Construction Bureau found that there were many obstacles to suddenly changing the long-standing practice of free vehicles. After explaining the reasons to the province, requesting that the free status be continued, the Finance and Construction Departments subsequently instructed that the exemption be granted. However, the needs of each organization should be verified and the number of vehicles limited. If the free licenses are found to be transferred and used on privately owned bicycles, they will be revoked immediately and not reissued, and a fine of ten times the donation amount will be imposed. In addition, post offices, telegraph offices, and other guilds will be required to pay donations and obtain licenses from New Year's Day of the 26th year.

烟民自首踊跃

Opium Addicts Surrender Enthusiastically

The county government of this county, after receiving the order to conduct a general review of opium and drug offenders, has made active progress and achieved considerable results. It has also sent personnel to the countryside to carry out publicity, stating that all opium smokers who voluntarily surrender and undergo rehabilitation can be exempted from imprisonment. Otherwise, starting from January 1st of next year, opium and drug offenders will be executed by shooting. Therefore, in recent days, many opium smokers have enthusiastically gone to the county to surrender. In addition, the fourth batch of opium addicts summoned for rehabilitation in the third year of this county, totaling 130 people, aged between 40 and 44, must report to the county promptly from the 28th to the 31st of this month. Those who fail to report on time and evade the summons for rehabilitation will be arrested and forced to undergo rehabilitation, and then punished.

A German named Pingke came to Changshu with a Chinese translator for some business. On the 29th, they took a company chartered car from Changshu to Wuxi. The German drove the car himself. Unexpectedly, when passing through Yanxiang, a villager came face to face, and the car could not avoid him in time, causing a collision. The villager died on the spot with a fractured skull. Seeing that he had caused an accident, the German immediately returned to Changshu and surrendered himself to the Second Sub-station of the Public Security Bureau with a note. Later, the villagers also came to report that the deceased's name was Fan Chun, a villager from Luofu Township, 40 years old. After mediation, the German compensated 300 yuan for funeral expenses and compensation as a settlement. However, the county government still sent personnel to the countryside for inspection on the 30th. It is heard that the German is an engineer and resident manager of the Guanmida Baojieke Machinery Factory, currently at 170 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. He fully accepted the conditions put forward by the villagers and reached a settlement.

Marathon Race to be Held on New Year's Day 106

The Marathon Promotion Association of this city is organizing a marathon race, starting from 13 miles, with successive increments of 3 miles, totaling four increments to 22 miles. This allows participating racers to progress gradually, preventing them from being intimidated by the long distance and giving up. The first 13-mile race is scheduled for New Year's Day of the 26th year of the Republic (tomorrow). The initial registration had 156 participants, and with additional mail-in registrations, the total has reached as many as 160 people. Famous athletes such as Niu Hongquan, Wang Zhenglin, Lan Shijie, He Baoshan, Zhang Liang, and others are participating and competing. The race is scheduled to start at 8:00 AM tomorrow morning at the intersection of Brennan Road and Yidingpan Road in Western Shanghai. Education News

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Prohibits Borrowing for Construction and Additions 111

To Avoid Irreparable Consequences

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education instructed all counties that the construction and additions of county-run schools should be investigated for necessity by the county education bureau director or section chief, as well as the supervisor and educational committee. The situation should be reported to the bureau meeting or county government meeting (in counties without a bureau), taking into account the actual state of the county's education funds, making overall arrangements, and preparing various attachments and requests for funds to be submitted to the province for approval and allocation of funds. If public funds are insufficient and the school must raise all or part of the funds itself, construction and procurement must wait until the funds to be raised have been collected, and the approved public funds must be received before proceeding with construction and procurement. As for the construction and additions of private schools, the funds required should be the responsibility of the school board to raise themselves. It is absolutely not permissible to disregard the economic situation, borrow heavily, and be burdened by interest, falling into a state of being unable to maintain operations. However, it is often found in county fund request cases that county school principals and private school board members and principals arbitrarily borrow heavily for construction and additions, making it impossible to remedy. The principal and interest on the debt gradually increase, leading to an unmanageable situation. County schools then request the bureau and county to issue funds for maintenance, while private schools request to be taken over by the county to transfer the debt. Such trends directly harm local education funds and indirectly affect the stability of educational undertakings. If strict prohibition is not enforced, the consequences will be dire. From now on, county and private school principals or private school board members who disregard their economic capabilities and have no proper remedies, and arbitrarily borrow for construction and additions, should be instructed to manage the matter themselves, and the education bureau or county government may not subsequently request funds or allocate subsidies on their behalf. Private schools with such debts will not be taken over by the county until the school board has properly settled the matter. In addition to separate orders, you are to comply and instruct your subordinate bureaus, schools, and social education organizations to take note. This order.

— Celebrating New Year's Day

Group Bowing in the Morning, Recreational Activities in the Afternoon. The Municipal People's Education Hall on Wenmiao Road in this city, in order to solemnly celebrate the upcoming New Year's Day of the 26th year of the Republic of China, has drafted the following celebration measures: (1) On that day, a tall memorial arch will be erected at the entrance, decorated with lanterns and national flags, and displaying pictures of customs and etiquette. (2) The entire hall will be open as usual on the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd days, and will be closed on the 4th. (3) On New Year's Day, at 10:00 AM in the hall's lecture hall, a celebration and group bowing ceremony will be held, and Director Pan of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and Section Chief Zhang will be invited to attend the ceremony and give instructions. In addition to Director Xu Zexiang of the hall and all the staff, there will also be members of the hall's choir, Peking opera, harmonica, and martial arts teams, and all students of the people's school, approximately 1,000 people in total, all of whom will attend uniformly. (4) From 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM on New Year's Day afternoon, a celebration recreational activity will be held. (5) In order to awaken citizens' attention to the Gregorian calendar and expand the celebration, the hall has also prepared a large number of Spring Festival couplets, which will be distributed to citizens for posting at that time, it is said.

Finance: Gold Market Takes Advantage of Low Prices, Short Covering Exists 119

The gold market remained sluggish yesterday, fluctuating only by five corners for half a day. Major players still had no new developments, and the market was still in a state of settlement and short covering. In the early morning, overseas silver markets saw the pound rise and the dollar shrink. The forward silver price in Monterrey did not change. The price of raw gold in London fell by 2.5 pence, and exchange rates contracted. The Central Bank's official exchange rates for both the pound and the dollar were flat, and the customs gold unit fell by four li. The standard gold price was posted at 1149.3 yuan. The after-hours pre-market trading opened at 54.50 yuan to 5 yuan, with Da Decheng selling slightly. The opening was slightly lower in the morning. After the opening, short sellers covered their positions, slightly pulling up the price. Although spot dealers had supply, the price remained hovering. The HSBC's official exchange rates for both the pound and the dollar were flat, remaining stable at this time. The silver equalization tax did not move, and there was still eager selling after entering the market, with a slight dip at one point. However, there was a large amount of short covering at the low, and the price was soon pulled up. Thus, at noon, the price was still hovering. Here are the half-day market conditions:

The opening price was 1154.6 yuan, 0.2 yuan lower than the previous close. Chunyuan Yong, Shen Da Yong, Qiafeng Yong advanced to 4.9 yuan. Tongfeng Heng sold slightly, retreating to 4.7 yuan. Jingfu Qiafeng Yong fell back to 4.5 yuan, while Ding Kang Da Decheng covered positions, stalling at 5 yuan. Wanxing sold bars at a high price. The noon close was 1154.8 yuan.

The settlement price, based on the Central Bank's standard gold price, was lowered to 1149.3 yuan, about 5 yuan higher than the closing price. There were limited transactions in the market. In summary, Chunyuan Yong, Ding Kang, Da Decheng, Shengyuan Yong, Qingfa Yong, etc. were on the buying side, while Qiafeng Yong, Qian Changxiang, Jingfu, Yuan Maoyong, Wanxing, Tongfeng Heng, etc. were on the selling side.

The half-day market conditions remained sluggish, with the morning opening at 1154.6 yuan and the noon close at 1154.8 yuan. December Futures: Yarn and Cotton Delivery Volume and Process; Market Prices Frequently Reach Peak Levels; Delivery Volume Also Increases 124

Jinji brand yarn for December futures began trading on July 3rd of this year at a price of 205 yuan and 80 cents. At that time, estimated reductions in US cotton acreage and rising market prices, coupled with rumors of the issuance of circulating notes in this port, made people even more confident and prices rose step by step, reaching a peak of nearly 220 yuan. Subsequently, due to favorable weather conditions in our country and a bumper cotton harvest, cotton prices fell, and selling became more active. The financial sector turned from long to short positions, breaking through the 200 yuan mark. Later, in the autumn, with bountiful harvests of agricultural products nationwide and booming cloth trading, various groups actively came to purchase for the autumn sales season. Factories had no spot yarn supply, and first bought up all 30,000 bales of yarn stored in yarn and cloth warehouses. The booming yarn sales set a new record for the past five years. More recently, factory labor strikes and severe Qingdao strikes made short positions even more apprehensive, and market prices soared, reaching a maximum of 268 yuan, the highest price since 1918. The final closing price was 263 yuan, a sharp increase of 57 yuan and 20 cents from the starting price. As a result, 17,750 bales remained to be delivered, an increase of 15,200 bales compared to last month. The delivery price, calculated based on the last three days, was 263 yuan, an increase of 19 yuan compared to last month. The delivered goods consisted of 20s, 16s, and 10s yarn, totaling 7,700 bales, of which 10s coarse yarn accounted for 3,000 bales. It is reported that China Cotton Corporation exclusively accepted the goods, with Yong'an Factory delivering the most. The brokerage firm license numbers and quantities of the receiving and delivering parties are recorded below.

Standard cotton for December futures began trading on July 3rd of this year at a price of 41 yuan and 35 cents. At that time, favorable news from US cotton, a greater-than-expected reduction in cotton acreage, and a rise of 60 points per pound caused excitement in the market. In addition, the large rise in the yarn market led to a recovery in the closely related cotton market, and buying momentum increased again. Market prices rose step by step to around 44 yuan. Subsequently, on August 20th, the first report from the China Cotton Industry Statistics Association indicated that this year's rainfall in our country was uniform, coupled with the high cotton prices of the previous year, which expanded cotton planting areas and benefited from favorable rainfall, resulting in a national bumper harvest estimated at over 16 million dan. The market shook, and prices turned downstream to above 37 yuan. Until recently, brisk yarn sales led to continuous advances in market prices, and the cotton market followed suit, rising again to 44 yuan and 30 cents. The final closing price was 42 yuan and 90 cents, an increase of 1 yuan and 55 cents from the starting price. As a result, 64,300 dan remained to be delivered, an increase of 37,000 dan compared to last month. The delivery price, calculated based on the last three days, was 42 yuan and 50 cents, an increase of 2 yuan and 10 cents compared to last month. The delivered goods included Tongzhou cotton, Huoji cotton, and Shashi cotton. The brokerage firm license numbers and quantities are recorded below.

Reportedly, the government will sell 3 million bales below the spot price

Yesterday, US cotton opened with sluggish demand from foreign merchants and brokers. Long positions were unwinding, and prices for each month ranged from up one point per pound to down three points per pound. Selling interest was not strong, with only limit orders being sold. Afterwards, when market prices returned to 12.5 cents, buying interest was hampered, and the industry waited for developments in the overseas situation, fearing that cotton purchased with loans after the New Year would be sold off. Therefore, they adopted a cautious attitude. However, during the price decline, the industry still bought in. Finally, according to unofficial news, the government would sell 3 million bales at 25 points below the spot price, and selling pressure increased again. As a result, spot prices fell by 16 points, and futures prices fell by 16 to 25 points. UK cotton spot prices rose by one point, and futures prices fell by three or four points. Indian cotton initially fell due to selling by European exporters and brokers, but later short covering was overturned by arbitrage selling, resulting in increases of half a rupee for Pingor, and decreases of 1.25 rupees for Umla, and 0.75 rupees for Bai Luo Xi. The original telegram is recorded on the left (telegram dated 29th).

Also, according to a telegram from Bombay, the opening forecast for the 30th was 227.5 rupees for Bai Luo Xi, 207.25 rupees for Aomura, and 175.75 rupees for Pingor, all down 1.75 rupees.

Most Rangoon Cotton Shipped to Japan Last Week 127

Bombay telegram, 29th: The amount of cotton exported from Rangoon last week totaled 2,432 tons, of which 1,250 tons went to Kobe, 1,089 tons to Osaka, 54 tons to Yokohama, 29 tons to Liverpool, and 10 tons to Venice.

Piece Goods: Cotton Cloth Market Particularly Active in Futures; White Goods and Fine Cloth for February and March Are Already Sold Out 128

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market continued to be firm. Spot transactions were mostly speculative. Customer spot purchases were slightly quieter due to the year-end closing. After Japanese factories opened large numbers of futures positions, customer interest remained strong. White goods and fine cloth for February and March have already been sold out, and prices rose by 5 to 10 cents. Due to month-end lending in the spot market, a small amount of cheap goods were released into the market, and prices increased by 2.5 to 5 cents (per piece). The spot market atmosphere was weaker than the futures market. Color goods, Dongpi Juxiancun straight satin, 200 cases were opened by Qingdao Gang yesterday, price (per yard) 31.5 cents. Futures for February and March of Sijunzi Serge also soared (per yard) by one cent. Spot prices also rose by 5 to 7.5 li. Fine twill from this factory sold briskly, and prices also rose, increasing (per piece) by 5 cents from the previous day. Coarse cloth, coarse twill, and patterned goods were all stable. Blue cloth and colored twill were also raised in price by (per piece) one dime due to grey cloth. Velvet was falling in price due to off-season demand. The highest price for 15-pound Gengyu brand was previously 13.9 yuan, but has now been reduced to 12.8 yuan.

Grain: Thick Japonica Rice is Popular in Local Purchases 129

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were over 50 sources of goods from various groups, totaling 11,000 to 12,000 shi. Thin indica rice accounted for over 40 sources. Although the Tianjin, Qingyan, and other groups continued to handle 5,000+ packages of the product, the market had limited change. Thick Japonica rice was, conversely, scarce and local sales were rather robust, leading to an increase in price of 10 cents. Du Yang pointed rice remained similar to previous values, and the path to Yin Yuan rice broaded, resulting in a rise of almost 10 cents.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, sources of goods from various He Xia routes were sparse, approximately 20 sources. Local sales of white japonica rice, upper-middle tier goods, continued to be secured, but scattered sales and higher-priced transactions were quiet. The market situation for high-tier japonica rice was stable, with mid-tier goods in particular being tight. Conversely, white japonica rice was weak, with prices being down 3 to 5 cents. Early thin indica rice sales were average and prices were stable. Yang Du Bu pointed rice prices were fixed, and white yuan scattered sales were ongoing, with prices rising about 10 cents. The prices of all other goods were similar to the previous market.

Customer Indica Rice Sales Gradually Improving 130

Yesterday, the market for Customer Indica rice turned robust, and market prices showed a turning point. Though it was the end of the Gregorian calendar year, due to reduced arrivals over the past few days and goods being held en route, yesterday, there were even hoarders asking about purchasing. Both the Northern and Guangdong groups had over 1,000 packages in transactions, and Henan also had some volume. Local purchasing interest was high, and general market sales opened above 10,000, so prices rose by about 10 cents. Full-day sales opened with 5,040 packages of Jiangxi rice, 3,300 packages of Hunan rice, 2,075 packages of Wental Jiaxing rice. In addition, 500 packages of small, twisted rice from the local market were sold as aged goods. The production cost of small twisted rice must be 13 or 14 yuan, which is difficult to coordinate. Yesterday's market opened at 11.1 yuan, a price that was about 1 yuan higher than the price sold the previous day.

Twenty-Seven Cars of Futures Wheat Delivered 131

Yesterday, twenty-seven cars of spot wheat were delivered for futures trading, with No. 23 receiving sixteen cars, No. 11 ten cars, and No. 5 one car. Those delivering included No. 19 with eight cars, Nos. 24 and 45 with four cars each, Nos. 26 and 37 with three cars each, No. 2 with two cars, and Nos. 18, 25, and 39 with one car each. Eleven cars of soybean futures were received and delivered, with No. 6 and others receiving and No. 7 and others delivering. Three thousand five hundred dan of bean oil futures were received and delivered, with No. 45 and others receiving and No. 25 and others delivering. One thousand tons of foreign-grown sesame cake were received and delivered, with No. 41 and others receiving and No. 24 and others delivering.

Japanese Merchants Scour for Spot Ramie; Market Rises by Two Dimes; Bean Cake Also Rises Two or Three Cents 132

Foreign-grown sesame rebounded again. The previous day, Jardine Matheson inquired and bought 200 tons, at a price of 14 yuan and 65 cents, an increase of 5 cents from the previous market. Japanese merchants are making every effort to search for spot ramie, and the market has risen by more than 20 cents. It is reported that 550 packages of Shashi ramie, 300 packages of Henan net yellow ramie, 40 packages of Guandian ramie were purchased from the local market, and 69 packages of Linhuai Pass ramie were purchased. Currently, the overall situation is still one of demand exceeding supply, so the trend remains strong. Soybeans continued to rise by 2 to 4 cents, and oil mills and inland cart shops continued to purchase. Recently, the destination of bean cake has included the inland wheat fertilization and pig feed markets. Yesterday, it was estimated that over 8,000 pieces of cake were produced by various factories, and the market rose another one or two cents. Moreover, with the New Year approaching and the market closed for three days, people are confident and stable. Yesterday, 13 cars of Sipingjie soybeans and 2 cars of Bengbu soybeans were traded. Scattered sales in the local market and inland. Over 300 packages of Dingjiazhou soybeans, 600 to 700 packages of Hankou Zhazao soybeans, and 200 packages of Jiujiang winter soybeans.

Silk and Tea: Silk Market Less Active Than Before 133

Yesterday, overseas silk markets were closed for the New Year holidays and will reopen on January 6th. The New York silk market fell yesterday, with Japanese silk down 83.75 points and Chinese silk down 3 points. The exchange market for the near term fell 3 points from the previous day, and the far term fell 1.5 points. Lyon silk prices were stagnant and unchanged. The Shanghai silk market seemed less active than before. Overseas silk prices fell slightly, and Shanghai Western merchants' limit prices were harsh. Additionally, the year-end was approaching, so trading was quieter. Yili silk also had some movement yesterday, with the afternoon price at 620 yuan, a fall of approximately 5 yuan compared to the previous top-end market price. A total of 131 bales of domestic and foreign silk were sold yesterday.

Sugar Market: Foreign Sugar Rises with Production Prices; Guangdong Coarse White Sugar Transactions Increase Significantly 134

Yesterday, the sugar market suddenly tightened due to news of a rise in Dutch production telegrams. The association's set price for 24 grade coarse white spot goods was 21 yuan and 65 cents, up 5 cents. Transshipment goods initially opened at 6 yuan and 30 cents, then rose to 35 to 40 cents, an increase of 18 cents from before. East white sugar also rose. No. 4 spot goods were 21 yuan and 80 cents, up 15 cents. No. 8 was 21 yuan and 40 cents, up 20 cents. No. 9 YRO mark was 21 yuan and 20 cents, up 10 cents. Transshipment goods were 6 yuan and 10 cents, the same increase. The same number, mark, was 6 yuan and 67.5 cents, up about 10 cents. 80-cent increase was 6 yuan and 40 cents. No. 9 Dutch red KD mark spot goods were 16 yuan and 20 cents, and transshipment was 6 yuan, both up 10 cents. The local Zhenji No. 1 soft white sugar was 20 yuan and 40 cents, no up or down, with the remainder returned according to regulations. In the call, the Guangdong group opened over 200 packages of Zhu Qing sugar at 12 yuan and 40 cents, the Chaozhou group opened 10 packages of Yingqiu soft red paper sugar at 15 yuan and 70 cents, and also over 30 packages of special high-grade Tiqing sugar at 14 yuan. The Jian group opened over 200 packages of Diao Qing sugar at 12 yuan and 80 cents.

The joint venture company held its second exchange of Guangdong sugar futures this week. The total fixed amount of Shunde Factory Wuyang group white sugar was 11,675 packages at 21 yuan and 40 cents, and Shixin Factory was 6,407 packages at 21 yuan and 20 cents, both up 10 cents. All were exchanged successfully.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Xinghua Longan Sales Rebound 135

Xinghua longan, previously experiencing quieter sales, saw production prices falling back. It is reported that Shanghai sales have recently become active again. For genuine Xinghua South Water goods, such as the authentic Zhufu Yu Zheng Er brand, sold for 112 yuan yesterday. Xingquan was 54 yuan, Zheng Tu was 48 yuan, and Xing Ji was 42 yuan. Local purchasing occurs daily, and the trend is firm.

Metals: White Lead Wire Market Prices Surge 136

No. 16 to No. 20 white lead wire has recently seen a sudden revival in the market, so the market standard has risen again by more than one yuan. For example, No. 16 sold for 10 yuan, No. 17 for 9 yuan and 50 cents, No. 18 for 10 yuan and 5 cents, No. 19 for 11 yuan, and No. 20 for 11 yuan and 50 cents. The construction groups are purchasing heavily, and many inland groups are also specifying purchases. In recent days, overseas prices have soared to 11 pounds, an increase of one pound from before, which is the only reason for this phenomenon.

Special Report: Production, Sales, and Manufacturing of Qihong Tea (Part 3) 137

From the above table, the market price of Qihong tea is highest in May and June, as it is the time when new tea enters the market, and exporters compete to purchase it. After that, prices show a downward trend. Distinguishing by year, the highest price was in 1931, and the lowest was in 1928, which is due to the influence of fluctuating silver prices. The average price for each year was also highest in 1931 and lowest in 1929, but even in that year, the price per dan was above 100 yuan. This refers specifically to top-grade Qihong, so it is insufficient to represent the general monthly wholesale market price of Qihong.

The following is a table of the average price of Qihong per market dan, compiled based on the monthly sales prices published in the China Bank Monthly over the past five years:

Table of Average Market Prices of Qihong Tea in the Last Five Years (Unit: Yuan per Picul) 138

The trend of Qihong tea market price fluctuations in the above table is similar to that recorded in the Shanghai Commodity Prices Monthly. The difference is that the Bank of China compiles its data based on the total monthly transaction values, while the Commodity Prices Monthly uses the market price on the 15th of each month as the standard for compilation and only includes top-grade Qihong tea, excluding medium and lower-grade teas. This is the difference between the two tables. (To be continued)

Popular Lecture

Macris 139

— Fei Ren

— "It doesn't matter if we father and daughter die for the sake of thousands of people." —

Along the coast of eastern Fujian, countless massive rocks and reefs stand in the water. Sometimes they emerge to form clusters of small islands, and sometimes they submerge beneath the surface. If navigators are not careful, they will collide with them and shatter their ships into pieces. At the same time, these emergent islands often become lairs for pirates, who take advantage of the opportunity to plunder. Fujian is located at the crucial intersection of the East and South China Seas, and its winds and waves are especially treacherous. Things may be calm usually, but as soon as clouds gather, a fierce and dark storm can erupt immediately, overturning ships, or else smashing them against the reefs. Naturally, these dangers are always less during the day and can be guarded against, because there are always warning signs on the reefs, and experienced navigators can also read the clouds and wind. But at night, night is the bane of navigators on the Fujian seas!

The most dangerous place of all is a cluster of reef islands outside Zheyang Island!

Nature prepares hardships for mankind. Does that mean mankind should diminish their ambition to advance? No. In order to conquer it, mankind invented the use of lighthouses. The method is very simple: build a very tall tower on a larger island near the shore. At the top of the tower, burn a very large and bright light that can illuminate the entire sea surface for dozens or hundreds of miles. This gives navigators the same kind of bright security as daylight even when traveling in this dangerous area, so they won't encounter unexpected disasters. Because lighthouses are so important, the lighthouse keepers are also very important. He must have a simple family with no worries, he must be of a considerable age, and especially he must be physically strong and have no vices. Because of this, 50-year-old Merlin became the keeper of the lighthouse on an island outside Zheyang Island. He had no relatives except for his nine-year-old daughter, Macris. The father and daughter lived on that isolated island, accompanying the lonely lighthouse, lighting the great lamp on time every night, protecting the thousands upon thousands of passing travelers, rich and poor, young and old, and never failing.

Speaking of this father and daughter's past history, it was also very bitter. The father was originally a fisherman in Zheyang Bay. There were many fish in the bay, and this man was strong enough to haul nets weighing hundreds of pounds, and he could also dive into the water to catch sea cucumbers, shrimp, and shellfish. His business at the fish market was not bad. But as time went on, his business declined. At that time, there was too much seaweed being imported. Countless seaweeds and fish were shipped in every year from Ryukyu, Taiwan, and Japan. People used large ships to fish in the open sea, using large machines to raise nets and using guns to catch fish. There were very many people on the fishing boats, so there was no danger, and the results were very great. The caught fish were loaded onto transport ships and exempted from taxes by their governments. Sometimes even the shipping costs were waived. They were sent to China. Because of treaty relations, China could only collect very low taxes on these foreign goods, and sometimes they were even tax-free. Of course, these imported seafoods were much cheaper than the fish of Chinese fishermen. People all loved to buy them. Chinese fishermen risked their lives to catch some fish, which was the source of their family's food and clothing, and they had to pay very high taxes. When they sold the fish, they naturally had to charge more. In addition, the fish brokers also took a cut, earning some money, which made the fish even more expensive.

At that time, Merlin's family consisted of four people: his eldest son, his wife, and little Macris, who was only seven years old. They were all strong, except for Madam Mai, who was weak from giving birth too many times and could only do housework. Although little Macris was only seven years old, she had always lived on the sea with her father and brother. When the fishing boat went out, the father and son cast the nets, and she steered the boat. When her father dived into the water, she forced her brother to guard the boat, and she would jump into the water herself to catch some shrimp and crabs. Occasionally, if she wasn't careful and her hand got pinched by a crab, she would always clench her fist, turning her small face iron-gray, without saying a word. When her brother asked her, she would glare at him and say that he was looking down on her. She liked to use a harpoon to spear fish the most. Her father made a lighter harpoon for her, and the three of them fished together. Because the sea was full of reefs and dangers, they inevitably ran into trouble often. Sometimes there were accidents at the lighthouse, or the lighthouse keeper was derelict in his duty, or the tower was poorly built and blown down by the wind. Not only were there problems at night, but there were also bad things happening during the day. When the father and son encountered people in need of rescue, hearing cries for help, they would always row the fishing boat out. At this time, Macris bravely stood at the bow of the boat or extended the harpoon and pole to the people in the water, or she would jump into the water herself, never letting her father and brother get ahead of her. She was strong, and the seawater had tempered her muscles and bones. The dangerous life at sea had also nurtured her heroic and unyielding spirit, and she loved to work. She didn't know what danger was, and she didn't know that there were difficult things in the world. Therefore, although the environment was bad and life was insecure, with the support of the three of them, fishing was not absolutely impossible, if the new exploitation mentioned below had not occurred.

When politics are bad and society is unstable, the people suffer. There were originally pirates on the Fujian seas, all of them poor men without clothes or food, who were brave and fierce. At first, they occupied the islands and made a living by robbery. The water police stations, which were paid to do nothing and evaded their duties, were already lucky if the pirates didn't come looking for them, so how could they dare to offend them? It was best if the pirates were considerate of them and never disturbed the ships of those great men and generals, but only robbed merchants and extorted from some semi-poor, semi-rich travelers. The pirates' power grew, and they implemented a division of spheres of influence, occupying the sea lanes to become aquatic overlords. They ordered the coastal fishing households to pay sea taxes every month in order to fish freely. If anyone didn't pay, they would tie them up and beat them, setting a deadline for payment. If they didn't pay after the deadline, they would tie them to large stones and throw them into the sea. The fishermen could only obey the overlords, because they couldn't resist themselves, and they didn't have the equipment. If they reported to the officials, there was a risk of leaking information to the pirates.

The Mai family's days became even more troublesome because of this. At first, they didn't have enough clothes to wear, but eating wasn't a problem. Except for the sick and thin mother, the father and son were quite strong, and it didn't seem like they weren't getting enough to eat. Later, even eating became a bit difficult. Those who should eat four bowls ate two and a half, patted their bellies, and drank another bowl of water, and they felt like they could manage. There were also many times when they changed the rice that should be cooked into porridge. It was common for Fujian people to eat porridge instead of rice, but that porridge was really just mushy rice, not what these poor fishermen had in their pots. Reducing food did not alleviate the Mai family's difficulties. People who sell their strength don't have enough strength if they eat less, and their work also suffers. Little Macris's round face slowly lost its color, and her father and brother's brows were often furrowed. They owed a lot of taxes and debts.

One day, Macris's brother went out to sea alone, and he didn't return at night. Merlin took his daughter Macris and borrowed someone else's boat to row out to sea to search for him. He also went to the homes of friends and acquaintances and the taverns to inquire, but there was no news at all. Little Macris thought that her brother must have had an accident at sea. Relying on her own skills, she cried all night and wanted her father to go out to sea with her again to search, but her father ignored her. The two adults were a little worried, fearing that their son had not fallen into the sea but had been lost on an island. However, they didn't tell Macris this, and they coaxed her to sleep. The next day, they got news of their son from the tavern. Sure enough, the disaster of not paying the sea tax for three months had already erupted. The son was now tied up in the pirates' dungeon, and he had to pay the money within two days in order to get out. How could they deal with this? The master can't understand the plight of the slave, because he doesn't know that money is not easy to obtain. He only feels that you have money but are reluctant to take it out to pay taxes. This kind of malicious and treacherous heart is hateful and murderous. In reality, the slave has already reached the end of his rope. He can only borrow but cannot repay. Finally, people are unwilling to lend, and he himself doesn't dare to ask. Everything that can be pawned has already been used up, and it can't be saved to this point to relieve the disaster.

The result is known to everyone. Time and deadlines never forgive people and are unwilling to take a slow step for anyone. The pirates are as ruthless as time. The Mai family's son lost his life. When Madam Mai heard the result of her son's fate, she cried to death on the spot. The family of four was reduced to just an old father and a young daughter!

After this heartbreaking event, Merlin also gave up fishing. He took his daughter and left his old home. With the help of friends, he went to the water police station to become a patrolman. Because Macris grew up on the sea, her face grew sullen if she didn't see the sea for a day. She would get sick if she didn't row a small boat out to sea and stir up the waves a few times. The sea breeze and waves were her air. How could she live without these? As for the father himself, he would look at the vast and boundless sea, guarding the masts that had been broken by the mighty waves, and shed tears.

They didn't stay at the water police station for long before they retired and took on the duty of guarding the lighthouse. There were no residents on the island. There was only a very large tower standing tall in the clouds. At the top of the tower was a glass room with a large lamp with a strong reflection hanging inside. Standing under the light and looking out at the sea, the strange and dangerous small islands were clearly visible. The red markers indicating dangerous shoals and sands in the distance were all in sight. No ghostly secret dangers could be hidden at all. The person who lit this great lamp stood under the light of thousands of miles and watched with his own eyes as the large ships, loaded and bulging, broke through the white waves and roared away, leaving those scheming and treacherous reef islands to stare at each other, unable to move. He felt very comforted and very happy.

Merlin had struggled for half his life and lost his wife and children. He never expected that at this most heartbreaking time, life at sea could still give him a little meaning worth cherishing, and he was greatly encouraged in spirit. His daughter Macris was older than before and more sensible. In addition to rowing the small boat under the lighthouse with her father to go to sea, she herself could follow her mother's old method of washing the rice three times, putting it in the pot, and adding more than twice as much water to steam it. There were fish, shrimp, shellfish, and snails near the shore. She carefully scooped them up and cooked them according to her mother's method for her father to eat with wine. Behind the small house was originally a small vegetable garden. The father hated fishing, so he put his strength into planting green vegetables and turnips. When the father was planting vegetables, Macris would go to the well to draw water, bringing it up bucket by bucket without any effort. Finally, the father would say that it was enough and tell her to stand aside and rest. She would put her hands on her hips, stick out her chest, and say, "Huh, who's tired! It's just two buckets of water!" Then she would pick up a large wooden ladle to water the plants for her father. The father would ask, "Macris? How old are you this year?"

"Nine years old. What for?"

"Are you afraid?"

"Afraid of what?"

"Afraid of kidnappers kidnapping you, afraid of big fish eating you, afraid of falling into the sea and drowning."

"Huh, I'll hit the kidnappers with a paddle, I'll drag the big fish up with a net for Dad to drink wine; falling into the sea, huh, the sea can't drown people, people can swim, didn't I just run away?"

The father would lift his head and look at her and say:

"Thousands of people have drowned on big ships, child. We have rescued people before. Don't people know how to swim?"

Macris became worried and didn't say anything. The father was afraid of boring her, so he said:

"Are you afraid after all?"

Macris shook her head, squatted down, turned her father's neck, and said face to face seriously:

"Dad! With us guarding the lamp, will thousands of people still drown on the big ships?"

Dad said, "We can protect them at night, but how can we say about during the day?"

Macris was worried about this. Whether it was day or night, whenever she heard the wind blowing at sea, she would climb to her window facing the sea to look, to see if there were ships in distress on the islands in the distance. One day, before dawn, Macris was suddenly awakened from a dream by a great wind, thunder, and rain. She jumped out of bed and ran to the window to look. Although in the darkness of the fierce wind and thunder, the light of the lighthouse still shone with flames in all directions, illuminating the entire sea. In the distance, she saw what appeared to be broken masts and a wrecked ship near Broken Heart Island, and she vaguely saw things crawling there, like people. She turned around and ran to her father's room, and saw her father sitting on the bed wrapped in a quilt, facing the window. Lightning flashed across his face, which was extremely painful and frightening. Macris ran up and grabbed her father, saying:

"Dad! Get up, go! Go save people!"

Merlin slowly turned his face, touched Macris, and said:

"Child, this wind and rain are very strong, I'm afraid we can't go."

"No, no, we must go! With us guarding the tower, we can't let people die on the big ships! Why should they die? No, go save people! Go save people!" After saying this, she ran outside with tears streaming down her face. Her father immediately jumped down, grabbed her, and put clothes on her, saying:

"Okay, good child, we'll go. It doesn't matter if we father and daughter die for the sake of thousands of people!" As he said this, he put on his clothes, put on a life buoy, packed up the boat, and walked down to the boat. The sky was gradually brightening, but the wind and waves had not diminished. The father and daughter tried their best to support the small boat, struggling forward in the surging waves. Sometimes they were thrown into the air by the waves, and sometimes they fell down as if they were falling into a deep valley. The rain and waves washed over them, and their clothes and hair were all soaked. Finally, relying on their expert skills, they steadily drove the boat to Broken Heart Island. The father climbed ashore, and Macris parked the boat in a sheltered place. Next to the island lay a half-sunken wrecked ship, revealing half of a chimney. There were some scattered objects and several floating corpses drifting on the sea, which were also being thrown and beaten by the waves, without any resistance at all. After a while, Merlin carried a person from the island, followed by many people, all with emaciated faces and broken clothes, hanging wetly on their bodies. They all got on the boat. Those who had been injured were carried on the back and laid on the bottom of the boat to drive back to Liudao. Macris, regardless of fatigue, quickly took out her father's clothes for everyone to change, and she hugged firewood to make a fire so that everyone could roast their clothes. She made the food in her house for everyone to eat their fill. She also served those who were injured in the same way, jumping in and out, talking and laughing, amusing those who had suffered misfortune and lost their relatives so that everyone liked her, calling her their savior and their god of joy.

According to the survivors of the shipwrecked ship, because the steam boiler was broken, the ship could not move easily. When it encountered wind and waves, it lost control even more and was blown onto the island, hitting a large reef. The entire ship was shattered, and only these twelve people who were rescued this time were left out of several hundred people on board. These twelve lives were completely saved by Macris and her father's willingness to sacrifice themselves. Everyone spoke of it with gratitude and sadness, not knowing how to repay them. Night came, and Merlin fell ill because he was too cold. Macris alone arranged places for many people to rest, and she groped in the great wind and rain, climbed up the high tower, and still lit that great light that rescued people from suffering.

Publishing World

"A Year-End Summary" 140

— Yu Po

Culture and Construction, December Issue

After reading the December issue of the Culture and Construction Monthly, published this year (Republic of China Year 25) by the Culture and Construction Monthly Society, we feel that the society's enthusiasm and achievements in engaging in Chinese cultural construction work are very commendable. This is not a blind praise; we only need to look at the articles in the December issue of the journal to believe it without a doubt.

Among all the articles in the journal, the most important topic is of course the "Year-End Summary" type of articles. There are six articles in total: (1) Jia He's "Sino-Japanese Relations in the Past Year"; (2) Wu Yugan's "China's International Trade in the Past Year"; (3) Zhang Sumin's "China's Finance and Fiscal Policy in the Past Year"; (4) Xu Xingchu's "Domestic Affairs and Foreign Affairs in the Past Year"; (5) Hui Jianyi's "International Political Relations in the Past Year"; (6) Xiao Ai's "The Newspapers of Beiping and Tianjin in the Past Year." The first and fourth articles are descriptive and reporting articles; in addition to describing the true historical facts, the authors also point out the correct views on the issues, which can be used to dispel foreigners' misunderstandings and fallacies about our country. The second and third articles are research and statistical articles, and they also fulfill their duties. As for the sixth article, it can be said to be a very rare piece of research material; it analyzes the changes in the newspapers of the Beiping and Tianjin areas and the oppression they have suffered from powerful enemies very clearly, so it is a very meaningful and valuable work.

In short, we are quite satisfied with the above six articles; especially the first and sixth articles can be called the best achievements among them. Other articles, such as Fan Zhongyun's "The Suiyuan War and the International Situation," Li Jianfang's "On the Chinese Communist Party and Its Recent Transformation," and Li Hengzhi's "Impressions of the Japanese Publishing Industry," can also be said to be very worthwhile to read. In conclusion, we are still satisfied with this issue of the Culture and Construction Monthly. However, we hope that the journal will have to expand its materials in the future; because in addition to political, diplomatic, economic, and other issues, there are other equally important issues in cultural construction work, such as religion, art, and science. These matters should not be ignored in practice.

The Publishing Industry and New Year's Cards 141

— Tian Zhiqi

New Year's cards are a kind of gift to celebrate the New Year. They have many styles and literary styles, and like human beings, they have expressions of childhood, adolescence, and adulthood. In short, they convey friendship between human beings with diverse, beautiful, elegant, and fresh postures.

Therefore, every New Year, the publishing industry produces a large number of New Year's cards to supply people's needs. Because human hearts are fond of novelty, the patterns of New Year's cards are newer year after year, truly changing in a myriad of ways, countless.

Although there are many patterns of New Year's cards sold on the market today, after careful inspection, there are not many that are truly good-looking. There is also a kind of New Year's card that is bought from abroad, and the quantity actually accounts for the majority. The cards are all in English, and naturally there is not a single Chinese character. Although that kind is prepared for Westerners, the quantity it occupies is always too large. At the same time, many compatriots also take pride in using this kind of style, so Western New Year's cards are prevalent in our country, and this has become a common phenomenon today. In fact, in all fairness, this is also a kind of self-humiliating policy of our own culture, that is, the strong color of the people of a semi-colonial area. Therefore, we feel that although New Year's cards are a small matter, we should also hope that they can be transformed to create various new and meaningful styles that can fully express the consciousness of customs and culture and the concepts of the country and the nation, or the improvement of personal and group life and the knowledge of new things, etc. Therefore, I believe that the publishing industry should pay more attention to the following items in terms of text and images for the production of New Year's cards in the future:

(1) Aphorisms of Famous People Past and Present—The aphorisms of sages and worthies of China in the past dynasties provide very detailed instructions on the way to conduct oneself in the world, the way to treat people, and the way to deal with things. Many of them are as precious as gold and stone, and can be regarded as the standard for self-improvement for life. It is especially appropriate to select their essence and print them on New Year's cards to guide friends to introduce each other, which will naturally be of great benefit.

(2) Portraits and Photographs of Famous People Past and Present—There are many materials in this regard, such as famous sages, philosophers, politicians, writers, scientists, revolutionaries, and other people who have virtue, integrity, and achievements in history and are believed by the people, all of which can be used for printing on New Year's cards. We believe that they can give people many inspirations and encouragements.

(3) Historical Sites and Cultural Relics—Our country has thousands of years of long history, and the famous historical sites left by each dynasty, such as the Great Wall, the Temple of Heaven, the Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum, the Summer Palace, the Tengwang Pavilion, or important cultural relics, etc., are all excellent materials.

(4) Famous Scenery and Unique Products of Various Provinces and Cities—There are even more materials of this kind. China is indeed not lacking in famous mountains and rivers, the Milky Way in the Three Gorges, the natural barrier of the Shu Road, the setting sun over the Yellow River, the Yangtze River like a piece of white silk, the towering Mounts of the Five Sacred Mountains, Huangshan, Mount Lu, Tiantai, Yandang, Emei, the scenic spots of Mount Tiantai, Yandang, Emei, and the Sun and Moon Mountains, and the filming of the famous products of various places, such as forests, minerals, rice, millet, fruit trees, cattle, and sheep, etc., are all very interesting, and you can gain a little common sense in a pleasant and joyful way.

(5) Filming of Famous Calligraphy and Paintings Past and Present—There are so many materials about calligraphy and paintings in our country that they are countless. Famous works such as landscapes, figures, flowers, birds, insects, etc., and the legal scripts of ancient and modern people can be selected for filming and printing. In addition, excellent modern woodcuts, oil paintings, etc., can also be selected. In short, those with an aesthetic or touching appearance can be printed.

(6) Photography of Great New Buildings in Modern China—In recent years, China's various buildings have made great progress, and great buildings such as the Qiantang River Iron Bridge and the Shanghai Sports Stadium can be photographed and printed on cards, so that the people can see their miniature, on the one hand, they can have many admiration for the country's construction, and on the other hand, they can also use this as a yearning, which is naturally very necessary.

The above are just a few examples, all of which are sufficient materials for making New Year's cards. Using New Year's cards to promote our own national culture and instilling a little good knowledge and feelings at the time of New Year's happiness is welcomed by everyone. Therefore, the publishing industry in China today must take on this mission that is usually not noticed by the public. This is a small opinion I have about New Year's cards.

Yuan Changying's "The Peacock Flies Southeast" and Others 142

— Kui Feng

"The Peacock Flies Southeast" (II)

As for the depiction of the characters' personalities, perhaps the author focused on their inherent viewpoints. The true personalities become obscured in the overly elaborate dialogues. Zhongqing's cowardice and incompetence, and Jiao's mother's isolated irritability, are relatively well-written and can be considered relatively successful. However, it is a pity that we do not see a deep and resolute personality in Lanzhi, the tragic protagonist who deserves the most sympathy. Some may think that describing personality as deep and resolute is too arbitrary. However, a person who is willing to suffer and dares to sacrifice cannot endure beatings for love, nor can they face death for love, without a deep attitude and a resolute will. Although she ultimately became a sacrificed weak woman, she had a price for her sacrifice, and that price is the eternal spiritual victory.

D. Some Points for Discussion

(I)

Regarding the characters, a few opinions have been briefly put forward in the previous paragraph, that is, Lanzhi's character is written too weakly and is too obscure. Perhaps this is due to differences in the author's personal understanding. Of course, the writer cannot force agreement. However, this is an opinion worth pondering. The smartest people in the world are madmen, and the bravest people in the world are those who commit suicide. If a person has the courage to make the final decision to commit suicide, that courage can enable them to do many things that others cannot. Suicide is not passive, let alone a sign of weakness. Lanzhi's ending was to automatically invite Yiqing to die together. Before her death, she was not without hope, so she could endure pain that others could not bear. This is not to say that Lanzhi should be portrayed as a shrewd and decisive woman, absolutely not. Rather, it is to say that in Lanzhi's actions and words, even though she is shedding tears and lamenting her fate, there should be a force that expresses her unique personality. This is the life that the playwright gave during the writing process, and now I am putting it forward as an opinion, which may be difficult for people to understand.

(II)

I don't know the author's place of origin, but it can be asserted that the author's "mother tongue" should be the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, with the accents of Hubei and Hunan being the most common. This kind of accent permeates the entire play's lines, which is a small shortcoming. This is not to obliterate regionalism. Sometimes, in order to cope with the current environment, a play written entirely in local dialect is specially written, but this is an exception. Since the nature of spoken drama extends to the whole country, it is best to use Mandarin Chinese as the dialogue.

(III)

The most taboo thing in a complete script is soliloquy. The playwright would rather insert a little more events and characters to express the part that needs to be a soliloquy in a roundabout way. The shortcomings of soliloquy are, first, it constrains the actor's expression, and second, it cannot gain the audience's sympathy. Because, since it is a play, the audience absolutely hates direct plots, which are both boring and dull. (To be continued)

Local News

The 26th Anniversary of the Founding of the Republic of China to be Held Tomorrow; Commemorative Meeting to be Convened at the City Chamber of Commerce in the Morning; Representatives from All Walks of Life, Seamen's Party Department, etc. to Hold Separate Meetings and Group Greetings; Three-Day Holiday; City to be Decorated with Flags and Festive Colors to Celebrate 143

The City Government, City Party Department, Seamen's Organizations, People from Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces, Lake Society, Ningbo Native Place Association, etc., will hold separate meetings and group greetings to celebrate the 26th New Year's Day and the anniversary of the founding of the Republic of China. The details are recorded as follows:

City Government

Since the serious national crisis, the Central Government has issued orders to suspend celebrations every New Year's Day in order to show its determination to work hard to strengthen the country. Now that the whole country is united and its international reputation is growing, it has been decided to issue a notice to hold a grand New Year's Day celebration. The Shanghai Municipal Government Security Team has prepared everything. On the New Year's Day of the 26th year, the Security Team will be inspected by Mayor Wu in front of the Municipal Government. Today is the Lunar New Year's Eve; Silver and Money Industries Handle Closing Accounts; All Banks and Firms Extend Hours Internally and Externally; Finance is Very Stable; Money Supply Remains Loose 144

Today is the Lunar New Year's Eve for the silver and money industries to close their accounts. All banks and firms are extending their working hours internally and externally. The bank clearing house is increasing the clearing once. The profits of all banks and firms will be collected and published by the association. The details are recorded below.

Two Industries Close Accounts

The closing of accounts in the banking industry has always been at the end of the Lunar New Year. The interest on savings deposits in the savings and commercial departments has been implemented one after another. Because the closing of accounts is approaching, the internal office hours yesterday were extended by two or three hours. Today is Lunar New Year's Eve, and the external office hours will be extended by one or two hours. The internal office hours will be extended until all accounts are cleared. The time for accepting bills in the money industry will be extended to 4:00 p.m., and the time for returning bills will be extended to 8:00 p.m. The internal office hours will also be extended until all accounts are cleared.

Increased Clearing

Since the establishment of the Bank Clearing House on January 10th, 1933, the member banks of the association have joined as clearing banks or entrusted the reserve committee to clear on their behalf. At the same time, the Central Bank has joined as a primary clearing bank. Today is the Lunar New Year's Eve. In addition to the usual clearing at 1:00 p.m. and 3:00 p.m., an additional clearing will be added at 5:00 p.m. As for the total clearing amount yesterday, it has increased to 10,469,396.71 yuan.

Financial Stability

This year, agricultural products in various places have been harvested, and various industries are very active. The loans issued by the silver and money industries, whether credit or mortgage, can be recovered on time. At the same time, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank are making every effort to regulate interbank finance and are lending as much as possible to relieve various industries. Therefore, even though yesterday was the day before the Lunar New Year's Eve, the Shanghai market's overnight interest rate still stood at 9 points per thousand yuan in both the morning and afternoon markets, which is very different from previous years, which is enough to prove the stability of Shanghai's finance.

Banks and Firms' Profits

After the annual closing of accounts, each bank will take a four-day holiday from the first day in accordance with the regulations of the association, including the end-of-year holidays. As for the profits of each bank, they will be reported to the association after each bank has calculated them, and then the association will collect and publish them. The large commercial banks can all make a slight profit. As for the money firms, they will take a three-day holiday from the first day. Although they will close their accounts once on the Lunar New Year's Eve, their final closing of accounts will still be on February 16th (i.e., the end of the lunar year). Therefore, the profits of each firm must be published by the association after the end of the lunar year, it is said.
