Wired Telegraph Between Shaanxi and Shanghai Was Opened Yesterday 151

Wireless Telegraph is Also Smooth

The wired telegraph between Shanghai and Xi'an was cut off after the outbreak of the Shaanxi Incident and has been blocked for nearly two weeks. Paramount Restaurant Creditors' Meeting Passes Settlement - 15% Cash Repayment Per Hundred Yuan, Submitted to Court for Approval and Supervision of Implementation 152

After the closure of the Paramount Restaurant, the debtor, Dacheng Company, immediately applied to the First Special District Court for bankruptcy. The court accepted the case and formally ruled the bankruptcy on the 30th of last month. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, the first creditors' meeting was convened at Jincheng Villa on Jing'an Temple Road. A Datong News Agency reporter has recorded the meeting details below:

Creditors' Meeting

Those present yesterday included Judge Jiang Gongliang from the First Special District Court, bankruptcy administrator Accountant An Shaoyun, debtor Zhu Hongru, and creditors with a total claim of over 262,000 yuan (the declared claim amount totals over 310,000 yuan). Judge Jiang presided over the meeting and announced the purpose of the meeting. Then, Accountant An reported on the total debt and asset situation of the Paramount. Finally, the debtor Zhu Hongru proposed a settlement plan. After the creditors discussed and amended it item by item, the whole body voted for approval. Judge Jiang then announced that the settlement plan had been approved by the whole body and would be submitted to the court for approval, after which the debtor would be supervised to implement it. The meeting adjourned at just after 4 PM.

Settlement Proposal

The reconciliation plan passed by yesterday's creditors' meeting is recorded as follows: "Upon investigation, the Paramount Restaurant operated by Dacheng Co., Ltd. suffered business failure due to the post-war economic downturn, and its capital was almost entirely lost. On July 10, 1936, a temporary emergency shareholders' meeting resolved to elect four representatives to fully represent all shareholders to find a better way to deal with the closure and liquidation. Unexpectedly, a case of more than 100,000 yuan in unpaid rent occurred, resulting in the execution and auction of the Paramount's assets, causing huge sacrifices and even greater losses. As a last resort, we had no choice but to request a declaration of bankruptcy. Hongru's sin is unforgivable. Fortunately, after pleading everywhere, a portion of cash was raised, so that 15 yuan can be obtained for every 100 yuan of allocated claim amount. It is clear that this method is originally difficult to satisfy people, but the people who lent the money declared that they were all committed to settling matters and helping to achieve coordination after bankruptcy. Only after the settlement is established can it be handed over to the bankruptcy administrator for legal distribution. It is not easy to obtain, and the opportunity is rare. Please, creditor gentlemen, give Hongru extra forgiveness and reluctantly accept it to bring it to an end. The settlement plan is listed below: Within two weeks after the establishment of the settlement, the debtor shall raise cash according to 15% of the claim amount and submit it to the bankruptcy administrator for distribution. The creditors agree to waive the remaining amount as final settlement, Zhu Hongru."

Fire at Jiru Lane, Girl Suffocated and Body Claimed 153

The Zhonghua Faji National Goods Umbrella Factory at No. 6 Jiru Lane, Jixiang Street, French Concession, was opened by Zhu Changfa (31 years old) from Zhenjiang. The business was relatively developed. The factory building was a three-story, two-up, two-down building with a wing room. Zhu's family also lived in the factory. At 0:35 AM on the 29th of this month, a fire suddenly broke out on the third floor of the factory, and a girl was suffocated to death. The details have been briefly recorded in the newspaper. When the fire broke out at 8 AM, factory owner Zhu Changfa and his family and workers were awakened from their sleep. Zhu first rescued two children and escaped. He then wanted to turn back to rescue another girl, Liu Fengying (13 years old), but was blocked by the flames and could not enter. The girl had already been awakened and wanted to escape, but was suffocated by the flames. The fire brigade arrived, poured water to rescue, and rescued the girl Fengying, but she was unconscious. She was immediately sent to Guangci Hospital, but died before treatment could be administered. The police sent the body to the autopsy office. The factory was extinguished after one hour of emergency rescue. The police sent detectives to investigate the cause of the fire and reported to Judge Wang Ren of the Second Special Court, who came to the scene with forensic scribes to verify the body of Fengying. Because factory owner Zhu Changfa surrendered to the police station for investigation and was unable to claim the body, the official ordered the body to be handed over to the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall to transfer the body to the family. Yesterday morning, Zhu Changfa, accompanied by the deceased's uncle Liu Yandao, requested the prosecutor of the Second Special Court to claim the body for burial. The request was approved. It is reported that the factory had fire insurance, and the loss this time was quite large. What was obtained could hardly compensate for what was lost.

Tong Hanchun Pharmaceutical Company Debt Lawsuit Trial 154

Tong Hanchun Pharmaceutical Company in Xiaodongmen has a history of more than 100 years and its business is thriving. It was managed by Tong Guangfu. In July 1932, it was sold to the Xu family in Hangzhou, and Song Fuchen was replaced as manager. Previously, when Tong Guangfu was the manager, the company owed the Minghua Bank a principal and interest of 39,386.45 yuan. The Minghua Bank went bankrupt, and its bankruptcy liquidator, Lawyer Li Mian, sued Tong Hanchun Pharmaceutical Company and Tong Guangfu, requesting joint and several repayment of the full amount. The current manager of the company, Song Fuchen, also hired a lawyer to appear in court, stating that the Tong Hanchun Pharmaceutical Company had been sold to the Xu family in Hangzhou and had been renamed Xingji, etc. Yesterday, Judge Pang held a trial. The plaintiff stated the facts and said that there was no proof of when Xingji was added. At this point, Tong Guangfu's lawyer stated that Tong Guangfu had deposited 250,000 yuan in the bank in the name of Maoji. The remaining amount was offset elsewhere, and there were still more than 50,000 yuan in deposit slips, which were sufficient for offsetting. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer said, "If there are such deposit slips, why not deposit them in the name of Tong Hanchun and Guangfu, etc.? Why deposit them in the name of Maoji? There is obviously a question that should be investigated further." At this point, witness Chen Caishao testified that he was formerly an accountant at Tong Hanchun and is now a counter clerk. It was formerly opened by the Tong family of the Renli, Renxiao, and Renti branches. The Renti branch is Tong Guangfu. At the end of July 1932, it was reorganized, and the new shareholders were Xu Kong, Shen, and others. The Tong family withdrew completely. The official ordered a postponement to January 9 at 1:30 PM for further hearing.

Lawyer Tao Gan Fined 155

Defamation Verdict

Lawyer Tao Gan, previously because Tao Longtu (reportedly his nephew) and Zhang Zhiman from Jiangbei were involved in a fraud case, Tao Longtu was sentenced to six months in prison by the local court. However, during the litigation, Tao Longtu's wife hired Tao Gan to send a letter to the Xinzha Branch to accuse Wu Yanling, the owner of Hengtong Hotel and a fellow villager, of robbery. After Wu was cleared, he sued Tao Gan in court for instigating false accusations. Subsequently, after the newspaper published a correction by Tao Gan, he pointed out that Wu was an illegal person who had been involved in trafficking people, etc. Wu then sued the court accusing Tao Gan of defamation. Yesterday, Judge Zhang ruled that Tao Gan spread words defaming others and fined him 100 yuan. If he performs labor service instead, it will be calculated at one yuan per day.

Letter to the Editor 161

To the Editor: We have examined the news item "State-owned China Merchants Bureau Opens Joint Transport, Exchange, and Delivery of Goods" published on page 11 of the third edition of your newspaper on the 8th of this month. The various articles listed in the "Notice to Merchants on Exchange" are inconsistent with the most recent regulations. The following corrections are made: 1. Direct ticketing for Shantou-Guangzhou joint cargo is still transshipped through Shanghai. 2. The handling fee for collecting the price of goods is slightly charged at 1% of the amount collected. 3. The latest regulations between the road and the ship stipulate that for water-joint cargo within the scope of the voyage, if losses are discovered, the ship bureau shall be liable to the cargo owner for compensation in the same amount as the railway department according to the "Regulations on Railway Cargo Transportation" issued by the Ministry of Railways, with the value of the goods at the time of shipment as the maximum limit. 4. For water and fire disasters, since July 1 of this year, the railway department has regarded the loss of goods due to fire as ordinary loss and is responsible to the cargo owner according to the regulations. The shipping company is now also preparing to be equally responsible for losses from water and fire disasters within the scope of sea transportation and is currently in the process of making regulations. Correspondingly inform you, I hope you will check and correct it to be in line with the facts and avoid misunderstandings. To show our friendship, to the editorial department of Shen Bao, China Merchants Bureau, December 29, 1936.

Shanghai Neon Light Manufacturing Industry (Continued) 166

— Chief Editor, China Credit

(Forty-First Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

In the spring of the 22nd year of the Republic of China [1933], J.L. Stellingweff and W. Stellingweff of Holland, along with others, raised ten thousand yuan in national currency to establish the International Neon Lights Co. Inc. U.S.A., setting up a factory at 36 Route Doumer [now East Huaihai Road]. In April of the 23rd year [1934], Chen Qiwei, who operated the Baiye Trading Company, founded the Dalai Neon Light Company. However, from the 22nd year onwards, the Shanghai market suffered from the impact of the global economic recession, and all industries were in decline. The neon light business was directly affected, and the business of various companies was far from what it used to be. The International Neon Lights Company, due to poor management, announced its closure in the 23rd year. The Fulaisheng and Huade factories had also stopped manufacturing neon lights and specialized in making light bulbs. The Tongming Company also soon stopped manufacturing and became a brokerage. The Xinguang, Meideng, and Ziguang factories reorganized one after another. Many other smaller factories went bankrupt. At this point, the neon light business was showing signs of decline!

Examining the comprehensive reasons, the impact of the economic recession was undoubtedly the main one, but there were also many other reasons. The scope of this industry could be large or small, and the cost of its machinery and equipment was less than that of other industries. Therefore, during the prosperous period of this industry, workers and staff of the larger factories, with a little savings, would set up their own factories, resulting in a proliferation of small factories and price competition. However, neon lights were relatively permanent goods, and merchants who could afford to install them had already done so. Furthermore, the business in other cities was unable to expand due to a lack of capital, resulting in a situation of oversupply, which led to the collapse of smaller factories and significant losses for larger ones due to competition.

Currently, there are fifteen companies remaining in the city, including Dongfang, Lian'an, Dalai, Dengmei, Xinguang, Ziguang, Datong, Guangming, Tongming, Da Shanghai, and Lihua. Among them, only Lian'an is still foreign-owned, while the rest are operated by Chinese. Dongfang is the largest and can be considered the leader in this industry.

Last year, Dongfang initiated the organization of the "Shanghai Neon Industry Trade Association" in the hope of coordinating steps and jointly seeking development. However, it ultimately failed due to other reasons. To this day, it remains in an unorganized state.

Three, Raw Materials and Manufacturing Methods

Neon lights are commonly available in four colors: red, blue, yellow, and green. The main raw material for their manufacture is neon gas glass tubing. Auxiliary materials include transformers, mercury iron shells, iron frames, copper, electric wires, etc., which are described separately below:

(1) Neon Gas - including hydrogen (Neon Gas), argon (Argon), and helium (Helium). Hydrogen is used for red, argon for red and blue, and helium for yellow. Green is made by combining two gases. Chinese manufacturers are unable to produce these three gases themselves. The gases used in this city are all imported from Germany and the United States, with American goods being the most common. They are sealed in bottles during import and are colorless and transparent, so they appear to be nothing. Each bottle contains approximately 1000 CC. The current market price is approximately 57.3 yuan per 1000 CC of argon, slightly less than 50 yuan for argon, and around 50 yuan for helium. Although there are slight fluctuations, the difference is still minimal. Local dealers include the De Fu Foreign Firm Chemical Department (formerly Yilideng Pharmaceutical Factory), Kefa Pharmacy, Yali Foreign Firm, and several others. Japanese companies can also produce neon gas, but there are currently no Japanese goods imported to the market.

(2) Glass Tubing - There are several types of glass tubing, with size 3 being the most commonly used. Those used in shop windows are thinner. The price is calculated by the pound, with an average price of around two yuan per pound (approximately ten feet long). Local glass factories such as Sanxing, Tongxing, and Zhongyang factories can all produce them. Except for Dongfang, which now manufactures its own, most factories use domestic goods.

(3) Electrical Transformers (Transformers) - commonly known as transformers, their size is calculated by the pound. Because the current used by neon lights is higher than that of electric lights, transformers must be installed, regardless of size, to produce light. Their quantity is also calculated by the pound. The largest used by neon advertisements in this city is 18,000 pounds, and the smallest is only 4,000 pounds. Both domestic and foreign goods are available on the market. Foreign goods are best from the Westinghouse brand. Local companies such as Bailu Foreign Firm, Qianxin Machinery Company, Kainengda Co., Ltd., General Electric Company, Kongshi Foreign Firm, and Siemens Foreign Firm all sell them. Larger factories such as Asia Electric Company, Yaguang Manufacturing Factory, and Huasheng Electric Factory can all produce them. Japanese goods are also imported, with lower prices, but they are said to be more prone to damage. The price of transformers is the most expensive of the neon light raw materials. Small ones cost tens of yuan, while large ones cost two to three hundred yuan. (To be continued)

Page 15

Indian Criminal Sentenced to Hanging Survives; Chinese and Foreign Funding Provided; Indian Criminal’s Wife Says Husband is Blessed by God; British Ambassador’s Telegram on Reduced Sentence Not Yet Announced; Western Newspaper Recounts Historically Interesting Events 167

The North China Daily News reported that an Indian man, Mr. Atma Singh, was being hanged in the Ward Road Prison on Tuesday morning when the rope suddenly broke. Although he suffered a brain injury upon falling to the ground, it was not serious, and he is expected to recover. He is currently in the police hospital. Reporters who went to the hospital to inquire about Mr. Singh’s reaction to not being hanged were unsuccessful, as hospital staff only stated that Mr. Singh was still alive and declined to comment further. This morning (Wednesday), a reporter from the North China Daily News visited Mr. Singh’s wife on Yulin Road. During the conversation, the wife was overjoyed, saying that her husband’s survival was entirely due to God’s blessing. Since her husband was convicted, she had firmly believed that God would bless the good and prevent him from dying. When asked about the broken rope, the wife replied that it was broken by the power of God. Her husband served in the police force and would pray in the temple for four hours every day, so this was his reward. The wife and her children are currently residing at a place that is not their home. The Singhs originally lived near the police station on Putuo Road, but after Mr. Singh committed the crime, the wife moved to a friend’s house. The wife also said that the authorities did not allow her to visit her husband, but she believed that her husband would recover because God would bless him. She said her husband would now be pardoned.

After this incident, the people of Shanghai were greatly surprised. The British and French Consuls-General in Shanghai, Sir Brenan, personally went to the Ward Road Prison this morning to investigate, fearing that the executioner had been derelict in his duty or had committed fraud. It is said that he intends to go again this afternoon. Some people are quite angry at the executioner for neglecting his duties. The authorities and prison officials are currently unwilling to disclose his name to protect him. It is said that he recently took a long leave and had only recently returned. According to the execution supervisor, the executioner was indeed absent-minded before the execution. It is also said that in September of this year, another Indian man was hanged in the Ward Road Prison.

The executioner's name was Mr. Gu Ding, who was an assistant at the time, but this time he was the main executioner. The rope used this time had been tested the previous night and was found to be very strong and suitable. Rumors from outside suggest that the rope was secretly replaced at night, but this rumor could not be confirmed as of this afternoon. It is said that only a small group of officials were present to supervise the execution. Many of them did not know what was happening until the executioner shouted, "Heavens, this is a tragedy!"

An accident occurred.

Mr. Singh is about four feet eight inches tall and weighs one hundred and sixty-four pounds. He is not particularly large, so it is unreasonable to say that the rope could not bear his weight. Mr. Singh was born in India in 1904 and joined the Shanghai Municipal Police in 1924. His service was generally considered conscientious. After British Consul-General Sir Brenan telegraphed the British Ambassador in Beijing, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, about the matter, it is said that he received a telegram instructing him to reduce Mr. Singh’s sentence. However, as of this afternoon, it had not yet been announced.

A reporter from the North China Daily News consulted legal experts in the city regarding this matter. They all believed that, according to the laws of various countries, the sentence should not be reduced or pardoned. If a person does not die after one execution, they can be executed again. Common people mistakenly believe that those who survive hanging should be pardoned according to the law, because historically, there have been very few people who survived hanging and were pardoned.

Now that Mr. Singh has been hanged but not died, British law does not explicitly state that he cannot be hanged again. However, this matter will be entirely decided by the British Ambassador. Although the law does not explicitly state that he cannot be hanged again, there are precedents for reducing or pardoning sentences. Forty or fifty years ago, in a certain place in England, a murderer was sentenced to hanging. The mechanism of the gallows suddenly did not work, so the person was not suspended in the air. The mechanism was repaired, but it still did not work. This happened three times in a row. On the fourth time, the warden announced that he did not want to

torture a living being.

So he released the person, who was later given a life sentence and eventually pardoned. He then became a publisher in London and became famous throughout the country for surviving three hangings. He died with considerable wealth. In the past, British doctors were allowed to take the bodies of those executed to conduct medical experiments. Once, a doctor revived the body of someone he had received. When the authorities found out, they pardoned the person. This is a

famous story

but it has never been verified. The Italian authorities in this city said that such an event would never happen in Italy today because people are executed by firing squad in Italy today. However, a hundred years ago, there was a person who was hanged but did not die and was pardoned. In Germany seven hundred years ago, during the feudal era, people were executed with a blade. The executioner’s job was quite difficult because if he could not sever the criminal’s neck with one stroke, he would be blamed and lose his own head. In America,

people are executed by electricity.

If a person does not die once, it can be done again until they die. However, in the past, when people were hanged, there was a person who was saved because the rope broke. It was later discovered that the person had been wrongly convicted because the real criminal had confessed. There is a Chinese story about a criminal who asked the executioner to cut off his hair first to test the sharpness of the knife. The executioner did as he was asked. The criminal’s family then rushed forward and shouted that the criminal only deserved one cut, and now that his hair had been cut off, his head should not be cut off again. The county magistrate was speechless and pardoned the criminal, punishing the executioner instead.

Reuters Shanghai, 30th. The British Consul-General in Shanghai, Sir Brenan, has instructed Reuters to publish the following announcement regarding the investigation into the case of the Indian man Atma Singh surviving hanging: "Today, the British Consul-General and a judge from the British Supreme Court for China inspected the case of Atma Singh surviving hanging in the Ward Road Prison, assisted by several rope experts. After detailed investigation and taking statements from many witnesses, the investigating committee is certain that the rope broke during the hanging due to unforeseen reasons. No one secretly replaced the rope. A detailed report on this case will be submitted to the British Ambassador to China soon."

From Beginning to End of Next Month

Jiang Customs Tax Office issued Public Notice No. 1558 to announce the re-registration dates for all customs brokers and domestic trading firms. All procedures for license renewal and bond must be completed within this limited period. Otherwise, they will be treated as unregistered, and the original licenses and bonds will be canceled. All trading firms are hereby notified. Tax Commissioner Bahrinson.

German Ship Sinks Cargo Ship 180

At 2:30 p.m. the day before yesterday, a ship carrying 310 bags of cake flour was waiting to be unloaded at Pier No. 6652, outside the Xianghe Steamer at Huashun Wharf in Hongkou. At that time, a German merchant ship arrived there. When the engine propeller turned, a huge wave surged up, and the cargo ship, because it was heavily loaded, was sunk by the waves. Many of the goods it was carrying were lost, and those that were not lost were completely submerged in the water, resulting in a great loss. That night, shipowner Huang Changlin reported it to the Water Patrol Police for filing.

If any kind person sees him, please send him to the Qian Yinshi Clinic at 52 Lane 6, Nanlinli, West Xinjiang Road, Haining Road for family reunion.

Mr. Chen Qiucao, director of the renowned artistic group White Goose Painting Society, adhering to his spirit of dedicated hard work, early in his career co-founded White Goose with his close friends Fang Xuegu, Pan Sitong, and others. Opening Hotels Under Business Names May Conceal Illegal Activities, Police Department Strictly Suppressing 183

The Police Affairs Department of the Public Concession Police Force has recently received reports stating that some individuals are opening small inns within the jurisdiction of the Old Gate Police Station. To avoid paying taxes and obtaining permits, they are not using the name of "inn" but are instead hanging signs with business names to evade the notice of the police. The department considers such incidents extremely dangerous because if these establishments harbor illegal activities, investigation becomes very difficult. Therefore, the department has ordered Lu Dagong, the Chinese detective head of the Old Gate Police Station, to investigate and suppress these activities. Detective Lu conducted separate investigations yesterday and discovered that the Tongyi establishment at No. 16, Lane 118, Zhejiang Road; the Yongkang establishment at No. 8, Lane 21, Hubei Road; the Taifengyong establishment at No. 54, Yuegui Lane, Guangdong Road; the Minkang establishment in the same lane; the Heyuanxing establishment at No. 10, Lane 47, Xishanglin; and the Tongshungong establishment at No. 10, Lane 438, Edward Road, are all disguised inns. He has ordered them to quickly pay taxes and obtain licenses, or face prosecution and sealing by the court. At the same time, one opium pipe, three opium lamps, fifteen opium pellets, and a can of ash were found in the Tongshun establishment, and they were immediately taken to the police station. Yesterday, a request was submitted to the First Special District Court for confiscation.

Tang Youren Assassination Case, Suspects Continued to be Interrogated Yesterday, Police Investigation Procedures Not Completed, Request for Extension of Interrogation Granted 184

Former Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, Tang Youren, from Hunan, was assassinated and seriously wounded to death on December 25th of last year in front of his private residence at Gan Cun, Gan Si Dong Road in the French Concession. The local authorities issued a reward for the arrest of the escaped perpetrators. Last month, the Shanghai Municipal Police Department, in conjunction with the Public Concession Police, arrested the main culprit, Liu Zhennan, at No. 228, Roberts Road, in western Shanghai. Additionally, the Public Concession Police arrested two robbers, Qiu Jiyu, and others in July. Because the incident occurred in the French Concession, the French Police sent detectives to transfer the suspects, Liu and Qiu, into custody and transported them to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention, pending investigation. During the investigation by the Fraud Bureau, the two suspects confessed to firing the shots that killed Tang and implicated their accomplices Yang Yousheng, Xiao Kaihui, Xiang Xingchang, Xu Zhimou, Tang Yongchang, and others, stating that Xiao and Xiang rented a house next door to Tang's residence to wait. This has been reported in this newspaper repeatedly. Yesterday morning at around 10 a.m., Wang Gangxu, the presiding judge of the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, continued the trial at the First Criminal Court, ordering Liu and Qiu to be brought before the court. Fei Xizhen, the lawyer from the Police Affairs Department, stated that the investigation procedures in this case are quite complicated and have not yet been completed. He requested an extension so that after completing the investigation procedures, he could request a trial. According to Qiu Jiyu's testimony in court, five shots were fired at Tang, hitting him. Yang Yousheng rented the house next door to Tang's residence, and Xiao, Xu, and Tang lived there. During the assassination, Tang and Xu were responsible for lookout duties. Liu Zhennan requested permission from the court to recount the events of the assassination. He testified that Yang Yousheng approached him to kill someone. He was a worker at a Japanese cotton mill who had lost his job due to oppression. His family, including his elderly mother, wife, and younger sister, were suffering. Because he was illiterate, he was temporarily moved and committed the crime. He asked the court to investigate. After reviewing the testimony, the court adjourned the trial to January 8th of the 26th year [1937].

In accordance with the annual settlement practices of each industry, which usually differ from January 1st of the Gregorian calendar by about forty days, to avoid misunderstandings, the association cabled your ministry on November 5th of this year, requesting a circular explanation for compliance. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce."

Representatives of Ninety-Eight Trade Associations Discuss the Implementation of Income Tax, Yesterday Invited Three Accountants to Lecture at the Chamber of Commerce 187

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce is a place where representatives of various trade associations in the city use their spare time to exchange ideas and connect with each other. It has been established for seven years. Recently, with the implementation of income tax imminent, it specially convened a dinner meeting for its members yesterday to discuss the implementation of income tax. More than 100 representatives from 98 trade associations, as well as accountants Pan Xulun, Xu Yongzuo, Jiang Wanping, and others attended. Chairman Luo Qinghua delivered a speech first, stating that since the National Government announced the Provisional Income Tax Regulations and Implementing Rules, several months have passed, and the implementation date is approaching. Everyone knows that income tax is a good tax. Advanced countries in Europe and America use this tax revenue as a major source of national income. At this time when the country is facing serious difficulties and defending against aggression, funds are needed everywhere. Therefore, the financial authorities are introducing income tax at this time to enrich the national treasury, which is naturally understood by the people of the country. We, the people of industry and commerce, have always been patriotic and will naturally jointly support this good tax. However, since this is a new undertaking, and the calculation of income tax and the methods of collection are very complicated, if we do not prepare in advance due to the immaturity of accounting in our country's industry and commerce, obstacles will inevitably arise. We may either bear unfair tax rates due to inaccurate calculations or incur charges of concealment and evasion due to incomplete records. The Chamber of Commerce, recognizing the great importance of this to industry and commerce, has specially invited colleagues to openly discuss it in order to promote the best possible implementation, so that the good tax can achieve its true name. The Chamber of Commerce has already started organizing a research group and welcomes all members to come to the Chamber of Commerce in their spare time to discuss together, hoping that after the implementation of income tax, we can achieve the good results of enriching the national treasury and maintaining the livelihood of the people. Next, Xu Yongzuo spoke on "The Understanding and Preparation that the Business Community Should Have Regarding Income Tax," Pan Xulun spoke on "Accounting Issues of Income Tax," and Jiang Wanping spoke on "Practical Estimation of Income Tax." The following are excerpts: Xu Yongzuo's speech, titled "The Understanding and Preparation that the Business Community Should Have Regarding Income Tax," stated that income tax is a tax levied on the income of the people, so it is the most reasonable, fair, and progressive tax system. Everyone has income, which means everyone pays taxes, so the tax base is universal and complete, and it is also flexible. However, the taxation procedures for income tax are extremely cumbersome, and the calculation methods are extremely complex. Therefore, we should not only strive to support it so that it can be implemented smoothly, but also have a deep understanding of the current system and make corresponding preparations. However, given the immaturity of the intellectual level of our country's people and the uncleanness of private accounts, it is not easy to achieve the best possible implementation. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, recognizing this, has jointly organized a lecture series with our firm to give public lectures. The Income Tax Affairs Office of the Ministry of Finance has also commissioned our office to draft tax payment guidelines for various types of income tax, as well as various reporting forms and valuation rules. After two or three months of research, we believe that in order to pay income tax, the industrial and commercial sectors should, in addition to having a thorough understanding of the current system, urgently prepare two points: one is the improvement of accounting books, and the other is the organization of capital property. The calculation of income cannot be fabricated out of thin air, and the reporting form, balance sheet, income statement, and property inventory must be based on clear accounts and vouchers. Otherwise, the tax office will directly determine the income amount, and even if it is unfavorable, there is no way to argue. However, with the accounting system and bookkeeping methods currently used by most merchants, it is difficult to achieve the goal of accuracy and clarity. Therefore, it is necessary to improve them in a timely manner. As for capital and public bonds, they are important components in determining the tax rate, and the verification of their amounts is very important. However, merchants in our country have not paid much attention to this point in the past. The actual investment amount may be greater than the capital amount on the books, and the actual property value may not match the value on the books. All of this has a significant impact on the calculation of income tax. Therefore, before the opening of the tax, it is necessary to re-estimate and thoroughly clean up. Pan Xulun's speech on accounting issues of income tax briefly stated that the calculation of the income tax amount is a relatively specialized issue. According to the income tax laws and regulations in our country, the calculation method for profit income is to deduct various business expenses and other deductible items from the total income of an organization. The remaining amount is the net income. Then, the ratio of the net income to the capital amount can be used to determine the tax rate and the tax amount to be paid. Therefore, accounting issues related to profit income can be divided into three categories. The first is how to determine the capital amount, the second is how to determine the total income, and the third is how to determine the deductible amount. However, these three categories of issues, judging from the income tax collection situations in various countries, seem to be full of complexities and changes. Therefore, industrial and commercial organizations in various countries often entrust accounting experts to handle tax matters on their behalf. This is similar to the situation in our country recently, where lawsuits are often entrusted to lawyers. Accountant Jiang Wanping spoke on income tax issues, stating that it is most important for taxpayers to pay attention to the integrity of accounting matters in order to ensure that all calculations are reasonable and legal. On the other hand, there should be proof of moderation in order to reduce the trouble of direct investigation by government offices. Therefore, the original draft of the income tax regulations had provisions for accountant certification, but due to the small number of accountants in our country, it is difficult to achieve universality, so it is temporarily difficult to formulate. However, we hope that those who cannot universally obtain suitable certification should still seek other ways to moderate. As for the procedures for reporting, confidential investigation, review, tax refund, and appeal, they should be as simple and convenient as possible to facilitate matters. Now that the implementation of income tax is approaching, there is not enough time to fully prepare for improvements. For urgent needs, it seems that each trade association should quickly unify accounting subjects and standardize the names of books and records based on the industry's situation. Then the bookkeeping procedures and processes will naturally be roughly determined, and they will be distributed to each trade for uniform use. Those who do not understand can consult with a specialist designated by the trade association or its accounting consultant for guidance. Various books and forms should be prepared monthly for month-end settlement, which can change the old accounting situation and gradually enter the path of rationality.

National Labor Maritime Conference Delegate Wang Zigang Hosted a Press Conference Yesterday to Report on the Proceedings 189

Wang Zigang, the employer representative who attended the 21st and 22nd International Labor Conference Maritime Meetings, returned to China and visited the authorities of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing on the 25th of this month to report on the proceedings of the meeting. He hosted a press conference at the Shipping Club at 4:00 PM yesterday to report on the proceedings. The following is a record of his report:

Once Every Three Years

Wang first stated that the Labor Conference discusses all industrial and commercial issues on land, while the Maritime Meeting specifically discusses maritime issues. The meeting was held on October 16th and closed on October 24th. The Labor Conference is held annually due to the complexity of the affairs, while the Maritime Meeting is held every three years. China first decided to attend the Maritime Meeting at the 13th session, with Chen Ganqing as the representative. This time, Wang represented China for the second time.

This Year's Meeting

The Maritime Meeting held a preliminary meeting last year to determine the agenda for this year's meeting. This time was the 21st and 22nd sessions combined because the League of Nations convention stipulates that all motions must be passed by two sessions before they can be established. The purpose of the Labor Conference and the Maritime Meeting is to seek equal treatment for land and sea workers. A total of over two hundred representatives from fifty countries attended the Maritime Meeting. Each country had four representatives, divided into two government representatives and one labor and capital representative each. Consultants and secretaries were appointed as needed. Each representative had one voting right. The government representatives from China were Li Pingheng and Bao Huaguo, the labor representative was Zhao Banfu, and the capital representative was Wang.

Five Major Proposals

There were five major proposals at this year's meeting: (1) regulations on working hours for seafarers and the issue of personnel allocation; (2) the responsibilities of shipowners to seafarers and the issue of seafarer illness insurance; (3) the issue of paid leave for seafarers; (4) the technical issues of officers and engineers working on ships; and (5) the equipment of each port for the safety, entertainment, and medical treatment of seafarers.

Form a Committee

During the meeting, a committee was formed for each issue to study everything. Each committee had government, labor, and capital representatives participating. At last year's preliminary meeting, the five proposals were distributed to various countries, and the opinions and proposals of various countries were compiled into draft conventions for discussion item by item. The first article was fiercely contested by European countries because it was related to international shipping and their interests were at stake. Wang participated in the discussion of the second and fourth articles because they were closely related to China.

Pass the Convention

Many conventions were amended and passed during the meeting, such as the convention on seafarer trainees, which originally stipulated fourteen years old as the youngest limit, but has now been changed to fifteen years old. All conventions passed are distributed by the Labor Bureau to the labor bureaus of various countries, requiring them to be submitted to the legislative bodies of their respective governments for approval and implementation within eighteen months, and to report the annual situation to the Labor Bureau (countries that do not approve the convention have no obligation to fulfill it). All normal international affairs are handled by the Labor Bureau.

Thoughts on the Inspection

Wang continued, stating that after the meeting, he went to France, Belgium, the Netherlands, the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries for inspection. There were two important impressions from this trip: (1) It is undeniable that our country's shipping industry is backward. The only solution is for all shipping companies to cooperate to strengthen the domestic organization and then seek to develop international shipping. (2) International shipping is related to import and export trade. National cooperation is necessary to develop outward. If national finances are solid and foreign exchange is balanced, then all matters will be easy to handle. If industries are divided and work is carried out without internal friction, then the future is infinitely hopeful. At present, various countries have a considerable understanding of us and are willing to cooperate with each other. For example, the United Kingdom sent Patrick, a representative for export credit loans to China. Wang met with him in England and hoped to help China develop international shipping.

Qian Dajun, director of the Military Affairs Committee Chairman's Office, and Zhu Shaoliang, director of the Gansu-Ningxia-Qinghai Pacification Office, flew to Shanghai on the same plane the night before. Zhu rested at his private residence on Masnan Road, while Qian entered Hong'en Hospital on Daxi Road that night for treatment. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Public Security Bureau Cai Jingjun, Commander of the Security Regiment Ji Zhangjian, as well as Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Qian Xinzhi, and others visited to offer comfort. Mayor Wu introduced Cao Chentao, director of surgery at the Shanghai Municipal Hunan Hospital, to the hospital for treatment. X-rays were taken twice yesterday morning to examine the extent of the lung injury. Following the doctor's advice that hospitalization was unnecessary, returning to his residence would be more convenient. Therefore, he was discharged from the hospital at about 10:00 AM yesterday morning and returned to his private residence on Haige Road for rest. Earlier, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited the hospital in the morning and was received by Ouyang Ju, chief of staff of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. He said that Qian's bullet wound entered from the left back, passed through the apex of the lung, and exited from the right shoulder blade. Qian received medication only at 11:00 AM, after being wounded at 4:00 AM in the morning, bleeding for six hours. Fortunately, he was physically strong and had strong resistance, so there was no major problem. Qian is still in good spirits and eating as usual, but the doctor instructed him not to see many guests in order to recover as soon as possible, so he can rest carefully. He will recover in a few weeks. Furthermore, according to Qian's family last night, the results of Qian's X-ray examination were very good. The injury to the apex of the lung was not critical.

New Movement Training Class Holds Graduation Ceremony; 179 Graduates 193

The New Life Movement Promotion Association of this city held a graduation ceremony for the students of the New Movement Training Class yesterday at 2:00 PM on the third floor of the Chamber of Commerce. A dinner party was also held last night at the Tongxinglou restaurant. The details are recorded below:

Guests Present

The graduation ceremony was held yesterday at 2:00 PM. The attendees included instructor Wu Tiecheng (represented by Pan Gongzhan), Chairman Pan Gongzhan, Chief of General Affairs Jiang Hao, Dong Ping from the Second Branch of the High Court, Cai Jinjun from the Public Safety Bureau (represented by Han Fen), Huang Boqiao from the Two-Roads Administration, Chen Chengshi from the Special Party Branch of the Two-Roads, Zhang Lianke from the Steel Plant of the Ministry of Military Affairs, Cheng Deyuan from the Seamen's Union, Yang Hu from the Songhu Garrison Command (represented by Lu Jingshi), Yang Zhonghan from the Special Party Branch of the Seamen, Sheng Juncai from the International Trade Bureau, Shen Xuejun from the Accountants Association, Qin Liankui from the Lawyers Association, and over one hundred students.

Chairman's Speech

After the ceremony began, Pan Gongzhan delivered a speech, stating that the New Movement Association held this New Movement Training Class. All the students usually serve in various agencies, organizations, and schools, and they took time out to participate. Now that the training period is over, they should put what they have learned into practice. Regarding this training class, he had two points to make: (1) In the recent days of national rejoicing and dancing, we expressed our support for the Supreme Leader. The Leader's support from the national populace stems from the influence of his personality and spirit. In recent years, the New Movement advocated by the Leader is a great manifestation of his personality and spirit. Therefore, to support the Leader, we must strive to promote the New Movement, making Shanghai, in both public and private life, do its best to make progress day by day. (2) During this time, you all studied and learned together, and you must have understood the theory of the New Movement and clearly understood the principles of the New Movement. From now on, you should work hard to put it into practice. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's preface to his book, "The Fundamentals of National Reconstruction", states that this book is not for reading, but is equivalent to the drill of infantry. The New Life Movement should not only be talked about, but also learned and practiced. Now that the work of purchasing is complete, we must all work hard to promote it, making public and private life in the city all transformed by the New Life Movement. This is the infinite hope I hold.

Report on General Affairs

Jiang Hao then gave a report on general affairs, stating that the training period of the association was two months, with 46 hours of instruction. The subjects included: (1) The Three Principles of the People and the New Life Movement; (2) The Theory and Practice of the New Life Movement; (3) The New Life Movement and the Cultural Construction Movement; (4) The New Life Movement and the National Economic Movement; (5) The New Life Movement and National Rejuvenation; (6) The Promotion of the Three-Part Plan and the Organization and Training Methods of the Labor Service Corps; (7) Music; (8) Air Defense Knowledge; (9) First Aid Knowledge. Regarding the occupational statistics of the students, 24 belonged to Party affairs, 39 to public affairs, 12 to public security, 15 to universities, 39 to middle schools, 36 to organizations, and 14 were recommended individually. Regarding academic qualifications, 50 were university graduates, 17 were university students, 64 were middle school graduates, 30 were middle school students, and 18 were unspecified, totaling 179 people.

Speeches by Guests

Commander Yang's representative, Lu Jingshi, gave a speech, stating that everyone here has studied the New Movement for two months and has a better understanding of it. Dr. Sun Yat-sen said that knowing is difficult, but doing is easy. Now that you all "know" the New Movement, it will be easier to "do" it in the future. Wang Yangming also said that knowledge and action should be united. Therefore, after "knowing", you must "act". The environment in Shanghai is filled with smog and foul air, making the promotion of the New Movement even more necessary. Therefore, you should all promote and develop the New Movement in the future, so that Shanghai can be replaced with a new vitality. If this is extended to the whole country, the nation can be saved. Director Huang Boqiao gave a speech, stating that China has a civilization history of five thousand years. All aspects of life are only well-spoken of in writing, but have not yet been put into practice. The New Life Movement proposed today is still to put forward the unique morals of China, so that everyone can follow them without deviation. He recently traveled along the Yangtze River and saw that the cities along the river have been焕然一新 compared to the past. This is the effect of promoting the New Movement. This is praised by both Chinese and foreigners. If all 450 million people can earnestly follow the New Movement, then no country in the world will dare to insult our country again, and our country will surely be strong. He is in charge of transportation and pays special attention to the New Movement. If traveling merchants can follow the New Movement, it will be more convenient to manage. Chen Chengshi and student Fan Zhenbang also gave speeches, with the length of the speeches omitted. Then the ceremony was declared over, and photos were taken before everyone dispersed.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Written on the Last Page 195

— Jia

Another year has passed! A set of new calendars has been torn to the last page from my hand, and another set of new calendars will take its place; and another set of days will be torn from my hand as it is now to the last day. Year after year, time flows away like water, and I only feel lost that I am getting old!

Although at the beginning of each year, I always set many wishes and plans, hoping to have a little bit of precious harvest in the new year, whether for myself, for society, or for the country. But life is too unsatisfactory, and wishes and plans seem like flowers in a mirror and the moon in the water. Only on this day of each year can I take a breath and move the unfinished work to the account of another new year.

But each time I fail, is it that my wishes and plans are too extravagant, or is it my own lack of effort, leading to this result? Here I don't want to defend myself. Every young person is ambitious and far-sighted. Their wishes and their plans, perhaps in another's eyes, are simply dreams, never to be successful. This, of course, I know very clearly. Young people only have success, not failure. Success is our responsibility, but failure is our shame! However, a warning sign stands in front of us—steadiness! You are not allowed to move. Thus, countless young people wander on detours, at a loss.

However, young people bear the heavy responsibility of being the future masters of the country. We not only hope for ourselves, but are also greatly hoped for. But no one saves us from detours and puts us on the broad road. Even if we accidentally discover the road to the broad road, it is our own people who prevent us from moving forward. Do you still want to plan? Do you still want to make wishes? It's the last day of another year!

"I wish I were blind! Let me grope in the darkness!" I remember these two sentences. But who wants to close their eyes? Looking ahead, I am making my hopes and plans again, today.

Street 196

— Shen Bing

The city street at dusk.

When the butcher shop no longer has bloody pig heads and the vegetable leaves in front of the small stalls are left for the chicks to peck at, the lines of the evening are even more blurred on the narrow city street. The wind is so strong, and the days in winter get dark so early.

On the quiet street, a wonton vendor walks by, tapping his clapper. The firelight in the stove sways in the wind, and a small bean oil lamp flickers. Several shy children stand next to it, their greedy eyes also flickering. A finger instinctively goes into their mouths to gnaw on, and their stomachs rumble somehow.

The wonton seller, like a wandering performer, scoops the hot soup from the pot, then slowly pours it back into the pot, teasing the children's appetites as he scoops it into the bowl. He looks at the greedy children proudly through the fog woven by the steam.

The children run away shyly, and when they return home, the side dishes for dinner are also delicious. The doors of the shops on both sides are gradually closing tightly: no, it is not people closing the doors, but the doors closing in the people.

The city street is even more melancholy, and there are still vendors selling late-night snacks, tapping their clappers, sparsely measuring the bottomless night.

Ferry 197

— Sheng Lu

Across the river, there is an old ferry, without an awning or oars, with a thin bamboo pole stuck there. An old man sits dozing under half of a cart shed, and he is the boatman who poles the ferry.

He never seems to get enough sleep, and he dozes off on the cartwheel whenever he has time. Or perhaps there are too few people crossing the river?

All around is a wilderness, and the wind whistles in the air, not knowing where it comes from or where it is going. The old man only feels that when a whistle blows, there is a cold air as sharp as steel needles逼进 from the thatched cracks of the cart shed, so he moves his seat slightly, as if this can make him warmer. His shy eyes also squint open a slit, looking to the opposite bank to see if there is anyone calling for the ferry. He also silently counts the copper coins he already has in his pocket, one, two, three...counting to eleven without further ado. The fare is one copper coin per person, so eleven people have crossed the river today. But no, he remembers very clearly that Huang Da Niang's son is sick, and Huang Da Niang crossed the river in the morning to go to Ba to ask a doctor. She said that she didn't have any change in her pocket, and she would pay when she came back. So he glanced at the opposite bank again. He still has the income of two copper coins!

The river suddenly roars, as if it wants to devour his old ferry. Gradually the waves roll ashore, perhaps even the only oxcart shed that can shelter from the wind and rain will be washed away? But the old man immediately wakes up. Today, gasoline boats are running from Dongjia Ditch to Gao Town. In the morning, there was also a series of "pa pa pa" sounds, stirring up the yellow mud at the bottom of the river, dyeing the river surface a scorched yellow. His ferry is like a kite with a broken string,颠来摆去 on the shore, and the bow of the boat is covered with sewage.

He watches the gasoline boat sailing from the east and heading west, so fast, like an arrow.

——If, he thinks, he had such a gasoline boat, it would probably only take two minutes to cross the river once, and he could stand at the stern of the boat without any effort, like an officer or something. He can't help but puff out his chest. He sees the person in the Zhongshan suit on the gasoline boat looking at the front of the river so smartly.

But that is a nightmare! After the gasoline boat passes, the river gradually stabilizes, the yellow mud also settles down, and the river water is as clear as a mirror. Under the sun, his broken boat is parked there, and even the shadow of the thin bamboo pole is lying quietly on the river surface.

This broken ferry often makes the guests who pay one copper coin to cross the river dissatisfied. "Why don't you make an awning?" They seem to blame the old man for not making the guests safe after collecting the fare. On rainy and snowy days, they have to stay at the ferry for half a day before the ferry slowly and weakly搖攏 comes over. Sometimes, when the old man is vaguely asleep, the guests crossing the river have to raise their voices to wake him up. When they get on the boat, they can breathe a sigh of relief and sit down, but the boat is also full of water, and there isn't even an awning. They look at the old man wearing a worn raincoat and think he is too comfortable.

"Humph! You are wearing a raincoat, but you let everyone get wet in the rain? Why don't you make an awning?"

To such questions, the old man can only勉强 laugh and say, "I'm poor! I want to save up a few more fares. Next year, I will definitely make an awning, next year I will definitely make an awning."

But he is already over fifty years old.

Someone on the opposite bank is calling for the ferry, and he puts down his dreamlike hope and stands up. He knows it must be Huang Da Niang coming back from town. Jumping into the boat, he uses the strength of his wrist from his youth, and he has already sailed halfway across the river in two strokes. Now he sees clearly that the person calling for the ferry is not Huang Da Niang, but a stranger. Although he feels that it will be dark soon if he waits any longer, this one copper coin business is still worth doing.

Back in the oxcart shed, the wind seems to be stronger. Why hasn't Huang Da Niang come back?

Someone is calling his name again, the voice is coming from behind, it is A Gen Ge, Huang Da Niang's neighbor. He says that Huang Da Niang came back from town on a gasoline boat, and she will send the fare tomorrow.

The sky is getting darker, and he can hardly see anything in front of him. Next year, I will definitely make an awning. This hope hammers heavily in his heart. The wind blows the whiskers under his chin, and he coughs.

Movie News

New Type of Comedy "The Sequel to Incarnation Girl" 202

The appearance of Incarnation Girl not only laid the foundation for Chinese comedy with the most beautiful posture, but also flaunted the audience with the most skillful techniques, so that the general public also believed that the Chinese film industry can also produce a perfect and interesting comedy. After the film was released, it caused a sensation everywhere, winning the welcome of a large number of audiences. The producer, Yihua Film Company, also produced a sequel, written by the original screenwriter Huang Jiamo and directed by the original director Fang Peilin, who spent eight months filming it. Yuan Meiyun plays the incarnation girl, and Han Lagen and Guan Hongda play Laurel and Hardy. In addition to the original cast from the previous film, three more stars were added: a glamorous star Lu Ming, a suave villain Wang Naidong, and a dull-witted Liang Dusheng. This created a gorgeous sequel, and the plot and acting skills broke the record of the previous film. It is expected to re-attract the audience of Incarnation Girl, allowing all movie lovers to get a real and valuable enjoyment of two hours. The film is scheduled to be released on New Year's Day at the Carlton Theater.

Time Cinema New Year's Issue Published 203

The Time Cinema New Year's Issue was published today. The content is more exciting than before. The sixteen-page photogravure pictorial is edited by Xi Yuqun and features new poses and new photos. The texts include topics such as the material problems of Chinese films and the breasts of female stars from the perspective of bodybuilding. Each copy is still sold for 2 dimes and is distributed by the Time Bookstore Company at No. 240 Avenue Joffre, Shanghai.

"Soaring Aspirations" Premieres Today 204

The highly anticipated film "Soaring Aspirations" premieres today at the Jin Cheng Grand Theatre in this city. This is a great work that Xinhua Company contributes to compatriots throughout the country during this extraordinary period. The story is based on a province in China, where farmers wage a heroic resistance for survival. This theme is undoubtedly extremely necessary in China today.

In terms of performance, director Wu Yonggang's past achievements are enough to guarantee your satisfaction. The complete cast, such as Jin Yan, Wang Renmei, Chen Juanjuan, Wang Cilong, Han Langan, Tian Fang, Li Mingjian, Zhang Zhizhi, and other popular actors, fills this film with a lively atmosphere. This is definitely something worth telling you all. In order to alleviate crowding, the theater will add a show at 10:00 AM every day from New Year's Day to the 3rd. Furthermore, "Suiyuan Frontline News," which Xinhua Company took great pains to film at risk, is also being screened simultaneously.

Cathay Screens "Silver Screen Scandal" 205

Mae West's New Work of Sensuality

Mae West can be said to be a unique beauty on the screen. She is not only good at acting but also writes scripts and dialogues. It is insufficient to merely view her through the lens of "flirtatiousness" and "romance." Like her previous films "I'm No Angel," etc., and "Go West Young Man," which opens today at the Cathay Grand Theatre, are all plays she wrote herself. In "Silver Screen Scandal," she plays the lead role, portraying a glamorous movie star. She feels that none of the men in the city are suitable for her. Later, she unexpectedly encounters a strong and powerful pilot in the countryside. She uses various methods to seduce him, but unfortunately, he is a man who does not understand romance, leaving Mae West feeling lost and confused. Her extremely unrestrained emotions and coquettish demeanor vividly depict the psychological experiences of a romantic woman. Such a good play can probably only be written and performed by Mae West.

Drama Workshop Actively Rehearsing "Sunrise" Ouyang Yuqian to Direct 206

Now that the national crisis is becoming increasingly profound, drama, the most effective weapon for organizing the masses, is experiencing a vigorous resurgence, despite being subjected to severe external pressure. This is naturally a good sign.

Recently, amidst the successive establishment and preparation for public performances by many drama groups, the "Drama Workshop," which has been in the works for a long time, has also announced its establishment. The main people in charge of the society are Feng Zi and Wu Tieyi, former leaders of the Fudan Drama Society. The sponsors include Ouyang Yuqian, Ying Yunwei, Zhao Jingshen, A Ying, Jin Xingyao... and others. Most of the basic actors are members of the Fudan Drama Society, and they are all quite familiar to the audience.

The first play to be performed by the "Drama Workshop" has been decided as Mr. Cao Yu's new work, the sensational four-act play "Sunrise." It was originally planned to have either Mr. Ouyang Yuqian or Mr. Ying Yunwei take on the role of director, but now, due to Mr. Ying's busy schedule, it has been decided that Mr. Ouyang will direct. They have been actively rehearsing in recent days, and it is expected that they will be able to meet the audience on stage in about a month.

"Sunrise" is Cao Yu's accomplished work completed this year. After its publication, the theater world acknowledged it as an even more successful work than Cao Yu's "Thunderstorm." "Thunderstorm" was first performed in Shanghai by Ms. Feng Zi and the actors of the Fudan Drama Society, and the director was also Mr. Ouyang Yuqian. Now that the entire team from "Thunderstorm" is performing "Sunrise," they are familiar with the work, and the future sensation can probably be predicted.
